People v. Perez


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


57 A.D.2d 560; 393 N.Y.S.2d 85; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11519



April 4, 1977 

 

1247 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Sharrock v. Dell Buick-Cadillac, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


56 A.D.2d 446; 393 N.Y.S.2d 166; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10485



March 28, 1977 



DISPOSITION: Order of the Supreme Court, Westchester County, entered September 15, 1976, modified, on the law, by adding thereto, immediately following the words "is in all respects denied", the following: "except that summary judgment is granted to plaintiff declaring sections 200, 201, 202 and 204 of the Lien Law to be unconstitutional." As so modified, order affirmed, with $ 50 costs and disbursements to plaintiff payable by defendants and action remitted to the Supreme Court, Westchester County, for further proceedings in accordance with the opinion of Mr. Justice Damiani.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from order of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Westchester County (New York), that denied her motion for summary judgment and for a determination that the action was a proper class action in plaintiff's suit seeking injunctive and declaratory relief and damages, contesting the constitutionality of N.Y. Lien Law §§ 184, 200, 201, 202, and 204.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sued for injunctive and declaratory relief, and damages after defendant enforced a lien on plaintiff's car by selling it at auction. Plaintiff contested the constitutionality of N.Y. Lien Law §§ 184, 200, 201, 202, and 204, which, inter alia, pertained to the sale of a vehicle to satisfy a garageman's lien. She made a motion for a determination that the action was a proper class action and for summary judgment. The lower court denied the motion in all respects. On appeal, the court found the only triable issue of fact presented related to the claims for damages raised by both parties. Sections 200, 201, 202, and 204 violated due process of law. The statutory scheme provided for prior notice of the sale. However, a garageman was authorized to enforce his lien for repair and storage charges by the sale of a car at public auction without affording its owner an opportunity for a hearing. Such a hearing, absent extraordinary circumstances, was an essential ingredient of due process. The actions of a private citizen could become the actions of the State for purposes of due process, as such actions did here. Class action relief was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The order that denied the motion for summary judgment and for a determination that the action was a proper class action was modified by granting plaintiff's motion for summary judgment to the extent of declaring certain sections of the New York Lien Law unconstitutional. As so modified, the order was affirmed, with $ 50 costs and disbursements to plaintiff payable by defendant and the action was remitted for a trial on the issue of damages.


HEADNOTES

Liens -- garageman's lien -- sale of automobile without hearing.

1. Sections 200, 201, 202 and 204 of the Lien Law, which permit the sale of a vehicle at public auction to satisfy a garageman's lien without providing a prior hearing to the owner, are unconstitutional. These procedures violate due process because of the [***2] total deprivation of the significant property interest involved. Under these enforcement statutes, no more than private gain is at stake, while, at the same time the sale of the bailor's car without a prior hearing could affect his ability to hold a job, making him a burden on family or friends. In fact, such a situation is present under the circumstances here where plaintiff, whose car was sold at public auction pursuant to section 200 of the Lien Law for failure to pay repair and storage charges, has alleged that her automobile is needed by her in order to seek employment, to pursue the family's everyday activities and to enable her to travel to nursing school. Accordingly, even though the statutory scheme provides for notice prior to the sale, absent extraordinary circumstances, due process requires that the owner be afforded an opportunity for a hearing where repair and storage charges may be contested.

2. The fact of the constitutionality of section 184 of the Lien Law, which statute confers a possessory lien in favor of a garageman on a motor vehicle lawfully in his possession for storage, maintenance or repair charges allegedly due, is not applicable to the question of the [***3] validity of the statutory scheme of the enforcement provisions, which permit absolute deprivation of use without a hearing as opposed to mere possession.

3. The execution of the garageman's lien constitutes State action and invokes consideration of due process concepts. The garageman, in executing his lien, is performing the traditional function of the Sheriff and is clothed with the authority of State law. Moreover, the fact that plaintiff's car was sold at public auction by a "duly licensed" auctioneer and, after such a lien sale title was to be registered by the New York State Department of Motor Vehicles only upon presentation of the auctioneer's bill of sale, accompanied by documentary proof of his right to sell the vehicle and a newspaper clipping advertising the sale, also involves State action.

4. Special Term was in error in denying a motion for summary judgment because of the presence of viable issues of fact. There was no dispute about the fact that defendant enforced a lien upon plaintiff's car by selling it at auction pursuant to section 200 of the Lien Law without affording plaintiff an opportunity for a hearing and, therefore, the only triable issue of fact presented [***4] relates to the claim for damages.

5. In view of the fact that subsequent complainants will be adequately protected under the principles of stare decisis, class action relief was properly denied by Special Term.

 

1248 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Gardner v. Lavine


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


56 A.D.2d 930; 393 N.Y.S.2d 51; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11330



March 28, 1977 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state social services commissioner sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court, Orange County (New York), which annulled his decision affirming a determination denying respondent applicant's petition for medical assistance. The trial court also declared N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 366(1)(e) and N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 18, § 360.8 to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: When the applicant was 19, he authorized his mother to convey shares of stock. Shortly before he renewed an application for medical assistance, he reached 21 and executed a second written instrument affirming the authorization to transfer the shares. The commissioner determined, after a fair hearing, that the applicant had failed to rebut the presumption in § 366(1)(e) that the transfer of stock was made for the purpose of qualifying for assistance and that the transfer had not been a normal transaction. The applicant appealed, and the commissioner's determination was upheld by the trial court. The applicant appealed again, and the court held that the statute and regulation at issue were constitutional. The court found that the applicant's authorization to transfer the stock was to repay an antecedent debt and hence was founded upon fair consideration. The court also found that the instrument making the conveyance clearly showed an intent to eventually authorize the stock transfer and was a "normal transaction," notwithstanding the date of the instrument that affirmed the transfer. The court held that either of those reasons was sufficient to rebut the presumption.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's judgment with respect to the constitutionality of the statute and regulation at issue and with respect to the determination that the action was properly brought as a class action. The court affirmed the judgment as modified.

 

1249 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Suffolk Outdoor Advertising Co. v. Hulse


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


56 A.D.2d 365; 393 N.Y.S.2d 416; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10446



March 18, 1977 



DISPOSITION: Order of the Supreme Court, Suffolk County, dated March 30, 1976 (and made in the first, second and third above-captioned actions) modified, on the law, by deleting therefrom the provisions which have the effect of denying the branches of the cross motions which sought dismissal of the first three causes of action asserted in the first above-captioned action and of the first cause of action asserted in the second and third above-captioned causes of action, and substituting therefor provisions dismissing those provisions of the said causes of action which assert the invalidity of the subject ordinance on grounds other than the assertion that the provision thereof which prohibits billboards is not reasonably related to public safety and welfare. As so modified, order affirmed, without costs or disbursements.

Order of the Supreme Court, Suffolk County, dated March 30, 1976 (in the fourth above-captioned action), as corrected by a further order of the same court, dated April 19, 1976, modified, on the law, by deleting the provision that the defendant's motion "is otherwise [***3] denied" and substituting therefor a provision that the said motion is otherwise granted by dismissing those portions of the first, second and third causes of action which assert the invalidity of the subject ordinance on grounds other than the assertion that the provision thereof which prohibits billboards is not reasonably related to public safety and welfare and that the said motion is otherwise denied. As so modified, order affirmed, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town sought review of the order of the Supreme Court, Suffolk County (New York), which failed to dismiss respondents, billboard owners', claims that the town's ordinance prohibiting billboards throughout the town was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court held that (1) the complaint set forth sufficient allegations to create a factual issue as to whether the ordinance provision was unconstitutional on its face because it did not reasonably relate to the public safety and welfare, (2) the ordinance was not in conflict with state policy, (3) the ordinance did not violate billboard owner's equal protection rights under the Fourteenth Amendment, (4) owners had not exhausted their administrative remedies provided for in the ordinance so be able to challenge the ordinance on the grounds that it was unconstitutional as applied to their property, (5) the administrative remedy as contained in the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague, and (6) there was sufficient provision for review of the initial determination made by the town board.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment and affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- sign ordinances -- aesthetic zoning.

1. Plaintiff billboard owners are entitled to a trial to determine if an ordinance of the Town of Southampton prohibiting nonaccessory signs constitutes an unconstitutional exercise of the police power by failure to reasonably relate to the public safety and welfare, since a factual issue exists thereto. A zoning ordinance is not invalid because its primary objective is aesthetic, so long as it is substantially related to the economic, social and cultural patterns of the municipality, is reasonably designed to promote government interests in that regard and so long as any distinction between accessory and nonaccessory signs is reasonably [***4] applied.

2. The ordinance does not violate the right to freedom of expression. Although the United States Supreme Court in Virginia Bd. v Virginia Consumer Council (425 U.S. 748) held that commercial speech is protected by the First Amendment, the case invalidated a statute imposing a total ban on publication of certain information and no considerations of aesthetics or other governmental concerns were involved. Unlike that situation and unlike handbills, billboards present a constant and unsightly intrusion which may be the subject of valid exercises of police power.

3. There is no merit in the contention that there is a State policy requiring compensation for removal of billboards, nor is there a denial of equal protection.

4. A contention that the ordinance is unconstitutional as applied to plaintiffs may not be raised until plaintiffs have exhausted their administrative remedies.

5. The amortization provisions of the ordinance are not unconstitutionally vague.

6. The absence of provision for review is of no significance, since judicial review is always available.

7. An action for damages does not lie, since municipalities are not liable in damages for enforcing an invalid [***5] ordinance.

8. No preliminary injunction is available, since the remedy is drastic and there has been no showing of a sufficient basis therefor in view of the exceedingly strong presumption of constitutionality of the ordinance.

 

1250 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Beame


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


56 A.D.2d 778; 392 N.Y.S.2d 444; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11050



March 15, 1977 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the City and the Mayor of the City of New York, sought review of an order from the Supreme Court of New York County (New York), which denied the municipality's motion to dismiss the cause of action filed against it for declaratory judgment by appellees, resident taxpayers and organizations devoted to the humane treatment of animals.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers and organizations sought a declaratory judgment that the city was operating certain of its zoos in violation of the Agriculture and Markets Law of New York, was committing common-law waste, and was violating the New York City Administrative Code. The taxpayers also sought a permanent injunction on the sale of animals and a summary inquiry. The pivotal issue was whether they had standing to bring the suit. The court held that the greater harm was not presented nor any reason stated why the courts were more qualified or given greater authority to run zoos than to run the transit system. Furthermore, the mere allegation of common-law waste did not alter the thrust of the action from one to insert the courts and litigants into management of public business. It was not sufficient for the taxpayers to allege, or even prove, they could have done a better job than the public officials as neither they nor the courts had been given that responsibility. The court reversed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, which denied the City of New York's motion to dismiss the cause of action filed against it for declaratory judgment by resident taxpayers and organizations devoted to the humane treatment of animals.

 

1251 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Isaacson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


56 A.D.2d 220; 392 N.Y.S.2d 157; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10051



February 25, 1977 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Steuben County Court (New York), which convicted him of the crime of criminal sale of a controlled substance in the first degree in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 220.43, a class A felony, and sentenced him to a minimum of 15 years to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a graduate student and teacher, was convicted by the court, without a jury, of sale of a controlled substance in the first degree. He was sentenced to a minimum of 15 years to life. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss the indictment in the interests of justice pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 210.40, that the evidence substantiated his defenses of entrapment and due process violations, and that the sentence imposed was cruel and unusual punishment. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court noted that the trial court properly exercised its discretion in denying defendant's motion to dismiss because the evidence of defendant's guilt was overwhelming and his motivation for the crime was personal profit. The court noted that the entrapment defense was not available to defendant because the evidence showed that he regularly engaged in a criminal enterprise. Defendant's due process defense failed because the police did not engage in over-involvement in the crime that reached a demonstrable level of outrageousness when they lured him to New York for the drug sale. Defendant's sentence fit the statutory definition of the offender class.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for sale of a controlled substance in the first degree, and affirmed the sentence imposed of 15 years to life imprisonment.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- controlled substances -- sale -- dismissal in interests of justice -- entrapment.

1. The trial court properly exercised its discretion in denying a motion to dismiss in the interests of justice ( CPL 210.40) an indictment charging defendant with the sale of a controlled substance. The evidence of defendant's guilt is overwhelming, his criminal activity reveals careful forethought and execution, and the record reasonably supports a conclusion that his motivation was personal profit. In addition, his testimony was not credible.

2. Evidence of other criminal acts of defendant shows that he was predisposed to commit the crime for which he was charged and, therefore, the defense of entrapment is unavailable to him. The fact that defendant was lured into New York from Pennsylvania by an informant is of no help to defendant as regards the defense of entrapment.

3. The conduct of the police did not reach such a demonstrable level of outrageousness as to result in a denial of due [***2] process to defendant. While the police are not to be encouraged to solicit foreign sellers of narcotics to set up shop in New York, their legitimate interest in the flow of contraband adjacent to our borders should not be foreclosed. Improper conduct of the police in their relationship with the informant does not violate due process rights of defendant and, although the police are charged with knowledge of the actions of their informant, the conduct of neither the police nor the informant shocks the sense of justice mandated by the due process clause.

4. The mandatory sentence provisions of section 70.00 (subd 3, par [a], cl [i]) of the Penal Law do not constitute cruel and unusual punishment and are not grossly disproportionate punishments. Both the defendant and his offense fit the statutory definition and the statute is not unconstitutional as applied to him.

5. Accordingly, the defendant was properly convicted of the criminal sale of a controlled substance in the first degree.

 

1252 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Portanova


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


56 A.D.2d 265; 392 N.Y.S.2d 123; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10427



February 25, 1977 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed the judgment from the Monroe County Court (New York), which convicted him of criminal sale of a controlled substance in the first degree and conspiracy in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant was convicted of criminal sale of a controlled substance in the first degree and conspiracy in the first degree. On appeal, he raised eight points of error. The appellate court found no support for defendant's claim that surveillance tapes had to be sealed in the presence of or by a judge. The court also found no support for the contention that all tapes in a certain exhibit had to be excluded. The court affirmed the conviction because no constitutional rights were violated in the plea bargaining and sentencing process. The court noted that there was no evidence that defendant cooperated with the authorities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed criminal defendant's conviction of a criminal sale of a controlled substance in the first degree and conspiracy in the first degree because no constitutional rights were violated in the plea bargaining and sentencing process that resulted in defendant's conviction.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- eavesdropping warrant -- sealing of recorded conversations -- chain of custody -- prejudicial statements -- plea bargaining.

1. The requirement of CPL 700.50 (subd 2) that recordings of communications be made immediately available to the issuing Justice upon expiration of an eavesdropping warrant and "sealed under his directions" does not require that the tapes be sealed in his presence. The sealing of tape recordings of conversations involving defendant was properly done by a member of the Sheriff's office at the office of the District Attorney.

2. There is no reason to conclude that the Sheriff's deputy upon offering the tapes into evidence did anything more than miscalculate when he stated that the sealed box contained seven tapes, although there were actually eight. The deputy's testimony that the box was in the same condition as when sealed negates any possibility of tampering, and there [***2] was a full foundation laid for the unchanged condition of the single tape utilized and the conversation offered in evidence.

3. The prosecution established the necessary chain of custody with respect to a second sealed box of tapes and one tape contained therein despite testimony that a detective, who did not testify, had one tape removed after the sealing, returned it and resealed the box. The accuracy and identity of the tapes was attested to, and it would be unduly burdensome to require the production of every person who monitored any conversation on any of the tapes. Even if the single tape removed were inadmissible, the remaining tapes were properly admitted and sufficiently support the guilty verdict, such that the admission of the single tape would be harmless error.

4. Both in the light of a testifying investigator's expertise and the general rule that lay witnesses may testify as to the doubtful, ambiguous or hidden meaning of statements made or heard by them, it was proper to receive testimony that, as used in a taped conversation, the word "cola" meant cocaine, "rocky" meant crystal or high grade cocaine, "mix" meant adulterant, "piece" meant an ounce of cocaine or heroin,  [***3] and the term "all in one", referring to money, meant $ 100 bills.

5. Testimony that the person who tipped the codefendant that a cocaine sale had been to Federal agents had died while the codefendant was in jail provides no basis for any prejudicial inference that defendant killed the tipster. The testimony exculpates the codefendant and does not implicate defendant or even indicate that the death referred to was by anything other than natural causes. Moreover, the question exists why defendant would wish to kill the person who warned him.

6. No prejudice resulted when the District Attorney elicited from the codefendant witness the fact that $ 50,000 bail had been posted, since nothing indicates that the District Attorney ever was aware of the form in which bail had been posted or by whom and defendant had arguably explored the matter by a question concerning the witness' financial condition.

7. Although a reference in the prosecution's summation to uncontradicted evidence of a certain telephone call improperly amounts to a comment upon defendant's failure to testify, that is not reversible error, since the court's charge sufficiently alleviated any detrimental effect.

8. The [***4] trial court acted within its discretion in refusing to accept defendant's plea of guilty upon the People's consent to the class A-III felony of criminal sale of a controlled substance in the third degree (Penal Law, § 220.39) in satisfaction of a charge of criminal sale of a controlled substance in the first degree (Penal Law, § 220.43), a class A-I felony, based upon the earlier exhaustion of all pretrial proceedings concerning a reduced plea and the defendant's refusal to plead guilty to a class A-II felony.

9. Defendant was not denied equal protection because he was not offered the option of pleading to a class A-III felony as was his codefendant, and his harsher sentence was not the result of his choice to stand trial. Defendant was convicted of a different crime than his codefendant, and there was no obligation to treat the defendant equally, especially in view of the codefendant's co-operation with the police.

10. It cannot be said that cocaine is irrationally classified as a narcotic drug, and the Legislature rather than the courts should deal with that issue.

11. Accordingly, defendant's conviction of criminal sale of a controlled substance in the first degree and conspiracy [***5] in the first degree should be affirmed.

 

1253 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Harvey & Corky Corp. v. County of Erie


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


56 A.D.2d 136; 392 N.Y.S.2d 116; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10031



February 18, 1977 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner concert promoters appealed an order of the Supreme Court, Erie County (New York) that granted the motion of respondents, county, stadium owners, and other promoters, to dismiss their petition pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 7804(f) that claimed a violation of equal protection under the Fourteenth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: The promoters contended that the stadium owners' grant of an exclusive franchise in a public facility that it owned violated the Equal Protection Clause when the exclusive privilege was granted to the other promoters without a reasonable, necessary, or appropriate basis. They did not allege that the county was actively involved in any sublease of the stadium. The court affirmed and found that the petition was deficient on its face because it failed to set forth the facts to be sifted and the circumstances to be weighed without which there could be no threshold determination of state action. The mere fact that the stadium owners were the lessees of public property was insufficient, standing alone, to show state action. The petition failed to allege facts demonstrating any cognizable unconstitutional deprivation of equal protection of the laws entitling the promoters to relief. The petition itself acknowledged that the stadium owners declined to sublease the stadium to the promoters because they found them unqualified and not sufficiently experienced to produce an out-of-doors concert at the stadium. Such explanation provided a rational basis for the denial of the sublease.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that dismissed the claim of the promoters against the county, the stadium owners, and the other promoters for a violation of equal protection arising from a sublease.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- equal protection of law -- sublease of county stadium -- monopolies.

1. In a proceeding by petitioners, who promote "pop" music and who sought to present concerts in Erie County's Rich Stadium, in which proceeding petitioners allege that they have been denied equal protection of the law and have had the free exercise of their business interfered with when the lessee of the stadium denied petitioners a sublease and granted a sublease to a promoter of "rock" concerts, the petition was properly dismissed. The petition fails to set forth facts without which there can be no threshold determination of whether there was a sufficiently close nexus between the State, in this case the County of Erie, and the private body, the lessee, so that the action of the private body may be treated as that of the State. The county had the authority to grant the exclusive right to the lessee to sublease the stadium and the [***2] fact the lease is of public property is insufficient, standing alone, to show State action.

2. The petition acknowledges that the lessee declined to sublease the stadium to petitioners because it found petitioners unqualified and not sufficiently experienced and that provides a rational basis for the denial.

3. Petitioners have not pointed to any controlling statute or administrative regulation requiring the lessee to sublease to them and courts should not question the allocation of resources and priorities of lawful acts of appointive and elective officials charged with the management of a public enterprise.

4. The petition does not allege adequate facts from which it can be determined that there was a conspiracy to violate the antitrust laws (see General Business Law, § 340 et seq).

 

1254 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bevilacqua


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


56 A.D.2d 605; 391 N.Y.S.2d 641; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10685



February 15, 1977 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the County Court, Westchester County (New York) on the State's charges of murder, robbery in the first degree, grand larceny in the third degree, possession of a weapon as a felony, possession of a weapon as a misdemeanor, and conspiracy in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, grand larceny, felony and misdemeanor possession of a weapon, and conspiracy. He sought review, alleging that the trial court improperly admitted into evidence his confession to the crimes. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court's ruling that defendant's confession was voluntarily made was correct. The court noted the trial court's findings that defendant was completely aware of what was going on and gave lucid and detailed answers, indicated considerable expertise as to his rights. The court found that defendant intelligently and knowingly waived his right to counsel on each of the occasions that his Miranda rights were given to him and that the admissions made, before counsel appeared on the scene were not subject to being suppressed. The court found no illegality or unconstitutionality in the taking of the oral confession from appellant and the notes thereof. The court said that defendant was 18 years old at the time of the interrogation and under all of the circumstances was fully capable of voluntarily and intelligently waiving his Miranda rights without notification to his mother.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on the State's charges of murder, robbery in the first degree, grand larceny in the third degree, possession of a weapon as a felony, possession of a weapon as a misdemeanor, and conspiracy in the first degree.

 

1255 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Subway-Surface Supervisors Asso. v. New York City Transit Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


56 A.D.2d 53; 392 N.Y.S.2d 460; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10016



January 31, 1977 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Kings County, dated March 9, 1976, modified, on the law, by (1) adding to the first decretal paragraph thereof, after the words "the New York Constitution", the following: "except that insofar as subdivision 1 of section 10 of the said act affects the calculation of pension benefits, it is in violation of section 7 of article V of the New York State Constitution" and (2) adding to the second decretal paragraph [***2] thereof a provision that the wage deferral agreement shall be subject to the provisions of subdivision 2 of section 10 of the Financial Emergency Act for the City of New York. As so modified, judgment affirmed, without costs or disbursements. There are no disputed findings of fact.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner union appealed from the decision of the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York), which ruled in favor of respondent transit authority and held that the New York State Financial Emergency Act of the City of New York (FEA), L. 1975 chs. 868-870 was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The union filed an action challenging the constitutionality of the FEA, which suspended wage increases due under a collective bargaining agreement. The trial court held that the statute was constitutional. On appeal, the court modified the judgment, and affirmed. The court rejected the union's argument that the statute unconstitutionally abrogated existing contractual rights by ignoring more feasible efforts to relieve the city's financial plight. The court concluded that the FEA expressly included the transit authority and that there was a reasonable nexus between the city and the transit authority. The court further determined that the statute's differing treatment of the payment of wages due to the transit authority's employees and the payment of indebtedness under municipal bonds and notes did not abridge the equal protection clause. The court noted that the debts owing to bond and note holders had the constitutional guarantee of the faith and credit of the city. The court ruled that the statute barring the calculation of the pension benefits on the wage increase effective under the contract violated N.Y. Const. art. V, § 7.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment by declaring the statute unconstitutional to the extent that it prevented the use of suspended wage increases in the computation of retirement benefits. The court affirmed the judgment, as modified, in the action filed by the union against the transit authority challenging the constitutionality of the Financial Emergency Act.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- wage freeze -- financial emergency.

1. In a proceeding by a labor union representing certain supervisory employees of the New York City Transit Authority, to declare unconstitutional provisions of the New York State Financial Emergency Act for the City of New York (L 1975, chs 868-870), enacted in response to the fiscal emergency arising in the affairs of New York City, which impose a wage freeze, suspending increases in the wages of employees of the city and of covered organizations, including the New York City Transit Authority, provided for in existing collective bargaining agreements, which suspension is not to be applicable in the event the employees or their collective bargaining representatives have agreed in writing to a deferment of the increases, the statute (FEA) is declared constitutional except to the extent that it prohibits the use of the suspended wage increases [***3] in the calculation of pension benefits. The pension rights of the members represented by petitioner enjoy constitutional status (NY Const, art V, § 7), in contrast to their rights to immediate payment of the increases in wages under their labor contract, and that constitutional status demands strict enforcement of the direction that those pension rights not be impaired.

2. There is a reasonable nexus between the city and the authority and, accordingly, the Legislature could treat the authority as an arm of the city and subject it to the same fiscal restrictions as those imposed on the city. That there might be more feasible methods to relieve the city's financial plight does not render FEA unconstitutional as in abrogation of existing contractual rights.

3. The difference in treatment accorded to the employees and to city bond and note holders, whose debts are not frozen but deferred to a new date of payment with interest, has a rational basis. Therefore, that difference in treatment involves no denial of equal protection to the employees.

4. There is nothing in the Federal Constitution or the Federal bankruptcy laws which bars the provisions of FEA.

5. To obviate any possible [***4] misunderstanding in a direction by Special Term that the authority offer the employees represented by petitioner a voluntary wage increase deferral agreement similar to those previously certified by the Mayor and/or the Emergency Financial Control Board, that direction is modified by adding a provision that the offer shall be subject to section 10 (subd 2) of FEA.

 

1256 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Franz


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


55 A.D.2d 424; 390 N.Y.S.2d 940; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9993



January 24, 1977 



DISPOSITION: Two orders of the Family Court, Queens County, dated March 15, 1976 and May 21, 1976, respectively, affirmed, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the decision of the Family Court, Queens County (New York), which found that the mother neglected her children after respondents, the City of New York Board of Education and representatives, filed a petition for neglect under N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 1012(f)(i)(A). The mother challenged the trial court's order of disposition.


OVERVIEW: The mother refused to send her children to school, and the trial court found that the mother had neglected her children under the Family Court Act. The trial court entered an order of disposition that discharged the children to the mother, and the mother was placed on probation for a period of one year on the condition that the children attend school. The mother challenged N.Y. Educ. Law art. 65 as unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order of disposition. The court held that the five-hour daily requirement for school instruction under N.Y. Educ. Law § 3210 was not arbitrary in nature and did not impinge upon any constitutional rights of the mother. The court held that the mother's argument that the New York Education Law impounded upon her fundamental guarantee of privacy was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that found that the mother neglected her children and that placed the mother on probation.


HEADNOTES

Parent and child -- neglected children -- failure to send children to school or provide equivalent education at home.

1. Because the yougest of her three children, then 6 1/2 years of age, was not doing well in reading and arithmetic at public school, a mother removed him from school and made sincere efforts to provide him with instruction at home which in her view was at least substantially equivalent to the instruction given at the school, as required by section 3204 of the Education Law, which also requires that instruction be given in 12 specified subjects, but she placed undue emphasis on subjects [***2] in which he showed interest, to the consequent neglect of other subjects, and she set aside only one and one-half hours per school day for his instruction as against the school's five-hour period for instruction, in violation of section 3210 of the Education Law, which requires that a minor attending upon instruction elsewhere than at a public school shall attend for at least as many hours. She later removed her other two children, then aged 11 and 13, from school, insisting she could teach them anything they needed to know. In the first of two separate proceedings instituted in the Family Court, the youngest child was declared neglected, after expert educators were called as witnesses for each side, and, in the second proceeding, in which the mother was faced with the statutory presumption permitting proof of neglect of one child to be admitted on the issue of neglect of any other child, and in which no expert witness supported her position, the older children were also found to be neglected. Family Court orders of disposition which discharged the children to the mother and placed her on probation on condition that the children attend school are affirmed.

2. The requirement of [***3] section 3210 of the Education Law that the period of instruction at home be at least the same as that provided by the school is not arbitrary in nature, nor does it impinge upon any constitutional right.

3. The compulsory features of the Education Law do not impinge upon the fundamental guarantee of privacy.

4. An argument that the compulsory feature of education has been debased to the point that it has become merely a compulsory attendance law and must be deemed unresponsive to the legislative purposes and intentions and set aside as unconstitutional is rejected.

 

1257 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Lublin v. Central Islip Psychiatric Center


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


56 A.D.2d 1; 391 N.Y.S.2d 603; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10014



January 24, 1977 



DISPOSITION: Two orders of the County Court, Suffolk County, both dated September 10, 1975, affirmed; order of the same court, dated September 17, 1975, affirmed insofar as appealed from, all without costs or disbursements.

Appeal from an order of the same court dated February 23, 1976, dismissed, without costs or disbursements. No appeal lies from an order which denies reargument.

Order of the same court,  [***2] dated January 8, 1976, reversed, without costs or disbursements, and proceeding remitted to the County Court for further proceedings in accordance with the opinion of Mr. Justice Shapiro.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient was committed to respondent psychiatric center after he was found not guilty of the crime of murder by reason of insanity. The patient sought a conditional release from the psychiatric center pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 330.20. The Suffolk County Court (New York) denied the patient a conditional release and he sought review.


OVERVIEW: The court found that § 330.20 was concerned with the commitment, confinement, and release of a criminal defendant who was acquitted on the grounds of mental disease or defect. The court further found that § 330.20 permitted the discharge of a committed person upon a determination that he would not be a danger to himself or others, but that § 330.20 did not address the respective burdens of proof in this matter. However, the court also found that, in denying the patient a discharge, the lower court held that the patient had the ultimate burden of establishing his lack of dangerousness and consequent right to conditional release from confinement. The court reversed and remanded the denial of the patient's request for release. The court held that, in requiring the patient to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that he was not presently dangerous to himself or to others as a condition of his being released from confinement in a mental hospital, the lower court infringed upon the patient's constitutional rights. The court further held that, upon remand, the State must undertake the burden to establish that the patient would be dangerous to himself or others if he were released.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that denied the patient a conditional release from the psychiatric center and remanded for a new hearing.


HEADNOTES

Mental health -- release from confinement after acquittal by reason of insanity -- burden of proof -- participation of District Attorney in proceeding for release.

1. Petitioner, who had been acquitted by reason of insanity of the murder of his wife and committed to the custody of the Commissioner of Mental Hygiene, who placed him in a psychiatric center, initiated a proceeding pursuant to CPL 330.20 for a conditional release, and, after a hearing on the issue of whether he might "be discharged or released on condition without danger to himself or to others", the statutory test for such release under CPL 330.20, the County Court denied his application, holding that he had the burden, which he failed to sustain, of establishing his lack of dangerousness and consequent right to conditional release. Its order denying him a conditional release is reversed and the proceeding is remitted to it to make a new determination upon the record made and upon such other proof as the parties may offer.  [***3] In requiring petitioner to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that he was not presently dangerous to himself or to others as a condition of his being released, the court infringed upon his constitutional rights. As the initiator of the proceeding, he had the burden of going forward with facts to raise an issue with respect to his lack of dangerousness, but the ultimate burden on that issue, which had not theretofore been judicially determined in any forum, rested upon the State. He met his burden of going forward in the first instance when he presented the testimony of two psychiatrists who treated him at the psychiatric center and the center's director, to the effect that he was not dangerous. The State then had the duty of meeting its constitutionally established burden of proving by a preponderance of the evidence that he was presently dangerous and that, therefore, it could continue to deprive him of his liberty.

2. The County Court properly authorized the District Attorney to employ two qualified psychiatrists to examine petitioner and testify at the hearing.

3. There is no merit to a contention by petitioner that the hearing should have been held in camera.

 

1258 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Carl A. Morse, Inc. v. Rentar Indus. Dev. Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


56 A.D.2d 30; 391 N.Y.S.2d 425; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10015



January 24, 1977 



DISPOSITION: Order of the Supreme Court, Queens County, dated February 6, 1976, affirmed, with $ 50 costs and disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to foreclose certain mechanics' liens, and for other related relief, defendants sought review of an order by the Supreme Court at Special Term, Queens County (New York), which denied a motion by defendants for partial summary judgment dismissing the first cause of action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff and defendant entered into a written contract for the construction of a warehouse. Subsequently, and within the time limited by statute, plaintiff caused to be filed against the premises four separate mechanics' liens for work, labor, and services rendered pursuant to the agreement. When a dispute as to payment arose, plaintiff commenced an action to foreclose its liens, whereupon defendant moved for summary judgment dismissing the first (foreclosure) cause of action on the following two grounds: (1) that plaintiff, having contracted and performed as defendant's agent, was not a valid lienor and (2) that N.Y. Lien Law § 2 was unconstitutional insofar as it purported to authorize the filing of a mechanic's lien without prior notice or the opportunity to be heard, thus constituting an impermissible taking of property without due process of law. The trial court rejected the latter contention, sustained the constitutionality of the statute, and found a triable issue of fact as to plaintiff's lienor status. The court was in complete agreement with the trial court's reasoning and conclusion; therefore, the court affirmed the order denying partial summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which denied defendants' motion for partial summary judgment dismissing the first cause of action.


HEADNOTES

Liens -- mechanics' liens -- constitutionality.

1. Article 2 of the Lien Law authorizing the filing of a mechanic's lien is constitutional. The filing of a lien does not result in the deprivation of any significant property interest and such minimal intrusion does not require prior notice or the opportunity to be heard in the context of due process of law. An owner is not deprived of the use or possession of his property including the right of alienation. While the lien impinges on the economic interests of the owner, the improvements had increased the value of the property by the amount of the lien, the lienor is required to state under oath the facts giving rise to the lien, the owner may discharge the lien by depositing the amount thereof into court or by posting a bond, and the owner can compel an expeditious determination on the merits. Accordingly,  [***2] the procedural safeguards in the statute effect a constitutional accommodation of the conflicting interests of the parties.

2. In an action to foreclose mechanics' liens filed by plaintiff for work, labor and services rendered pursuant to a contract for the construction of a warehouse in which agreement plaintiff was designated as "agent for the owner", a triable issue of fact exists as to the validity of plaintiff's status as a lienor.

 

1259 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Vickers v. Home Federal Sav. & Loan Asso.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


56 A.D.2d 62; 390 N.Y.S.2d 747; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10017



January 21, 1977 



DISPOSITION: Order unanimously modified in accordance with opinion by Goldman, J., and, as modified, affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant bank sought review of the order of the Supreme Court, Monroe County (New York) which directed that plaintiffs' suit for alleged violations of the Truth in Lending Act, 15 U.S.C.S. § 1601 et seq., be maintained as a class action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sued defendant bank for alleged violations of the Truth in Lending Act, 15 U.S.C.S. § 1601 et seq., and obtained certification of the suit as a class action. Defendant contested maintenance of the suit as a class action and objected to the method and content of notice to potential class members. On appeal, the court affirmed certification of the suit as a class action. Plaintiffs' claims for recovery of a statutory penalty were permitted under state and federal law. The court modified the order requiring notice because it was premature. Further discovery proceedings to identify potential class members were required. The court redrafted the exclusion request to convey a more balanced statement of rights and liabilities of potential class members. The court redrafted the notice of class action letter to be sent at the appropriate time.


OUTCOME: Certification of class action affirmed and order of notice modified. Under state and federal statutes, plaintiffs' claims for penalties against defendant bank for violations of consumer credit laws were appropriate for class action status. The court redrafted the exclusion request and notice of class action.


HEADNOTES

Actions -- class actions -- recovery of Federal statutory penalty.

1. Plaintiffs' action based upon violations of the Truth-in-Lending Act may properly be brought as a class action for recovery of the civil penalties provided in section 1640 of the Truth-in-Lending Act (US Code, tit 15, § 1640) on behalf of all persons to whom inaccurate disclosures were made by defendant over a one-year period. CPLR 901 (subd [b]) precludes class actions for recovery of statutory penalties unless the statute imposing the penalty specifically authorizes a class action, and section 1640 expressly provides that an action thereunder may be brought in any court of competent jurisdiction.

2. There is no need for a threshold determination of possible conflicts of interest between the class representatives and [***2] class members, and, although the amounts of damages may vary, there is a sufficient commonality of interest to warrant class action certification, since the elements of plaintiffs' causes of action are substantially identical to those of the class.

3. The proposed notice to class members should describe the class so that an individual can determine if he is a member.

4. There should be further discovery proceedings to identify potential class members prior to sending notice.

 

1260 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Modjeska Sign Studios, Inc. v. Berle


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


55 A.D.2d 340; 390 N.Y.S.2d 945; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9980; 9 ERC (BNA) 1766; 7 ELR 20259



January 20, 1977 



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment affirmed, without costs. Appeal by proposed intervenor-plaintiff dismissed, as moot, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sign owner filed an action against defendant Commissioner of the Department of Environmental Conservation in the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York). The sign owner was denied an injunction to restrain the enforcement of N.Y. Envtl. Conserv. Law § 9-0305. Intervenor outdoor advertising association's motion to intervene was denied. The commissioner's cross-motion to dismiss was granted. The sign owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The sign owner claimed that the commissioner was required to pay just compensation for the removal of the signs he owned that were located within 660 feet of federally-aided highways and that § 9-0305, which provided for an amortization period rather than payment of compensation, was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. Outdoor sign regulation was a proper and valid exercise of the police power. Legislation whose legitimacy was measured against an aesthetic purpose had have met the test of reasonableness. Outdoor advertising that offended the eye and detracted from the natural beauty of the setting were legitimate targets of legislation requiring their removal and the commissioner did not need to pay any compensation where signs were regulated pursuant to the state's police power. The police power extended to all the public needs and if the means employed to regulate existing offending signs were reasonable, there could be no objection to their employment on the ground that the rights of private property were thereby curtailed. A reasonable period of amortization to enable one to recoup his investment was constitutionally valid.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court granting the commissioner's cross-motion to dismiss was affirmed. The appeal by the outdoor advertising association was dismissed as moot. The issues concerning the denial of the motion for a preliminary injunction were moot.


HEADNOTES

Environmental conservation -- regulation of advertising signs.

1. ECL 9-0305, which prohibits the erection and/or maintenance of advertising signs and structures within the Catskill and Adirondack Parks without a written permit from the Department of Environmental Conservation, but provides that all such signs within the Catskill Park as of May 26, 1969 may be continued without permit until January 1, 1976, was enacted in a proper and valid exercise of the police power and is constitutional.

2. Section 88 of the Highway Law [***2] does not require the payment of just compensation for the removal of signs in the Catskill Park which are located within 660 feet of federally-aided highways. While the Federal Highway Beautification Act, in response to which said section 88 was enacted, declares it to be a national policy for States to seek to establish control of outdoor advertising by prohibiting erection and maintenance of such advertising in noncommercial areas, and further declares that any taking of such signs or structures by the States should result in the payment of compensation, it does not mandate the States to do so, but, in fact, provides for a 10% reduction in Federal highway funds if a State does not. The State can, and has, elected to cause offending sign removal within the Catskill Park by employing its police power and providing for a reasonable period of amortization as an alternative to the payment of compensation.

3. The State is not constitutionally required to pay compensation where signs are regulated pursuant to its police power.

4. Regulatory enactments such as ECL 9-0305 which advance legitimate governmental purposes and do not foreclose alternate channels of communicating the same information [***3] are not violative of the constitutional guarantee of free speech.

5. ECL 9-0305 seeks to regulate outdoor signs which offend aesthetic values, and such legislation is neither an improper classification of signs nor palpably arbitrary.

6. That ECL 9-0305 may deprive the owner of signs of income from a lawfully established business does not render it violative of the owner's civil rights.

 

1261 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Albany Police Officers Union Local 2841, etc. v. Albany


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


55 A.D.2d 346; 390 N.Y.S.2d 475; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9981; 94 L.R.R.M. 2670



January 20, 1977 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged the judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which confirmed the award of a public arbitration panel that had been established by the public employment relations board (PERB) following the request of respondent union pursuant to N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 209. The trial court directed the city to comply with the terms of the award.


OVERVIEW: The PERB designated a public arbitration panel as requested by the union to decide a dispute between the union and the city regarding conditions of employment of the city police officers. The panel granted some of the demands of the union. The trial court confirmed the award and directed that the city comply with the terms. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that contrary to the city's argument, the arbitration panel had accepted the city's evidence pursuant to N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 209(4)(c)(iii). The court held that the panel had not determined that the city could borrow money to pay the requested salary increases, as claimed by the city, but that it discussed raising taxes instead. Despite the city's contention that the panel improperly compared the police salaries in surrounding communities as a basis for the award, the court ruled that § 209(4)(c)(v) authorized such a comparison. The court concluded that the panel properly considered the statutory criteria for balancing the city's ability to pay with the interests of the employees. The court summarily dismissed the city's remaining arguments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the confirmation of the award of the public arbitration panel and the order directing the city to comply with its terms following the union's request for arbitration regarding employment conditions of the city police officers.


HEADNOTES

Arbitration -- public arbitration -- police officers.

1. An award made by a public arbitration panel, granting some of the demands of the union which represents a city's police officers, has a plausible basis and was properly confirmed. The arbitration panel accorded proper status to the city's proof, did not act in an erroneous belief that the city could borrow money to pay the salary increases directed, properly used a comparison of the salaries paid to police in surrounding communities, taking into account the higher ratio of police to population in the city and attempting to seek factors which would be subjected to a minimal effect by such ratio, gave due consideration to the city's ability to pay, and considered the statutory criteria for balancing the ability of the city to pay with the interests of the employees.

2. A portion of the award which directs the city [***2] to pay union officials for time devoted to union business does not constitute an unconstitutional gift of public money for private purposes.

 

1262 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. McLaughlin


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


55 A.D.2d 1000; 391 N.Y.S.2d 220; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10325



January 14, 1977 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a 17-year old, entered a plea of guilty to manslaughter first degree, a class B felony. The Supreme Court of New York sentenced defendant to a minimum of five years and a maximum of 18 years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state indicted defendant for murder, second degree, and a class A-I felony, criminal possession of a weapon in the fourth degree and unauthorized use of a motor vehicle. The trial court suspended the proceedings when defendant withdrew his request for a psychiatric examination and pled guilty to manslaughter first degree, a class B felony. On appeal, defendant argued that the provisions of N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law 720.10, subd. 2, that precluded youthful offender consideration of any youth indicted for a class A-I or A-II felony was unconstitutional. Defendant did not raise the invalidity of the statute limiting eligibility for youthful offender treatment on the highest count of the indictment until his appeal. Defendant also claimed that the trial court should have ordered the psychiatric examination before it accepted his plea. The sentencing court had a presentence psychiatric examination that described defendant as an alert, oriented, cooperative young man who was rational, coherent, and in contact with reality. The court held that: (1) defendant waived his argument on the constitutionality of the statute, and (2) the sentencing court properly imposed the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court unanimously affirmed the judgment of conviction and defendant's sentence.

 

1263 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Patno


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


55 A.D.2d 965; 390 N.Y.S.2d 468; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10278



January 13, 1977 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the County Court of Clinton County (New York), which entered judgment, upon a verdict, and convicted him of the crimes of attempted rape in the first degree and attempted sodomy in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted rape in the first degree and attempted sodomy in the first degree. At trial, the prosecutor made remarks in summation that tended to invoke a so-called "safe streets" argument, and he also suggested to the jury that its function was to convict. On appeal, the court held that although it neither approved of the prosecutor's remarks or condoned the propriety of making such a suggestion. The court found that the trial court's allowance of such comments was not reversible error, as the comments were made in response to the defense's attack upon the prosecution's witnesses and within the context of overwhelming proof of guilt. As the proof of defendant's guilt was virtually conclusive and there was no significant probability that the jury would have acquitted absent the errors, the summation errors were held to be harmless. Furthermore, the court held that the application of an evidentiary rule, N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 60.42, that excluded evidence of the victim's prior sexual conduct in sex offense cases, was proper. The trial, despite the earlier indictment, had begun after the statute's effective date. The judgment was therefore affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order that convicted defendant of attempted rape and attempted sodomy was affirmed. In light of overwhelming proof of defendant's guilt, the prosecutor's prejudicial comments made in summation were held to be harmless error since they were made in response to an attack upon prosecution witnesses. The trial court's application of an evidentiary rule was also proper, as the trial had begun after the statute's effective date.

 

1264 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Bauer v. Bauer


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


55 A.D.2d 895; 390 N.Y.S.2d 209; 1977 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10130



January 3, 1977 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of an order from the Family Court, Westchester County (New York), which directed him to pay child support as well as attorney's fees to petitioner mother in her child support action.


OVERVIEW: The father and mother were separated but not divorced. The mother brought a child support action, and the family court ordered the father to pay child support in an amount that was later modified. The father appealed, and the court reversed. The court ruled that it was error for the family court to have denied the father's request for an inquiry into the mother's resources under N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 414. Section 414 stated that the court had the power to apportion the costs of support of the child according to the parents respective means and responsibilities, while N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 413 provided that the primary obligation for child support rested with the father. The court determined that where both parents were capable of support, inquiry may have been granted as to the financial circumstances of both parents and that the father should not have been precluded from attempting to prove that the mother has her own substantial earnings even though his own earnings may have been adequate to have paid child support. The court summed up that the responsibility to support the child rested with both parents in proportion to their respective abilities to provide.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in favor of the father in the mother's child support action where the father was denied inquiry into the mother's resources.

 

1265 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Kew Gardens Sanitarium, Inc. v. Whalen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


55 A.D.2d 226; 390 N.Y.S.2d 256; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 15886



December 30, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Cross appeals were taken from a judgment of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which, in a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding, rejected petitioner hospitals' constitutional challenge to N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 10, § 86.9(d) and directed respondent Commissioner of the Department of Health to hold full hearings on waiver applications, considering only factors related to the reasonableness of hospital costs.


OVERVIEW: The challenged regulation limited reimbursements to hospitals by governmental agencies according to a formula based upon minimum utilization rates. The court found that § 86.9(d) was validly enacted pursuant to the agency's delegated discretionary power and that a hearing was not a prerequisite to the initial function of establishing rates. Moreover, the regulation did not violate the supremacy clause of the United States Constitution. The court determined that a hearing was necessary, however, as to each hospital's application for a waiver from the minimum utilization requirement. Rendering decisions on such applications was judicial action, and due process required that each hospital be given an opportunity to be heard and to present evidence to establish that a waiver was warranted. Denial of a waiver predicated on factors unrelated to the reasonableness of hospital costs was arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that required hearings on the hospitals' waiver applications.


HEADNOTES

Health -- certification of reimbursement rate for health services -- necessity for hearing.

1. The regulation (10 NYCRR 86.9 [d]), which, in part, limits governmental agency reimbursements to hospitals by a formula based upon minimum utilization rates of 60% for maternity, 70% for pediatrics and 80% for medical-surgical care, and which was formulated pursuant to subdivision 3 of section 2807 of the Public Health Law charging respondent commissioner with determining and certifying that the proposed rate schedule for payments to hospitals by governmental agencies are reasonably related to the costs of efficient production of health-related services, is constitutional. The certification of a reduced rate for health services prior to a hearing does not amount to a denial of due process. The establishment of rates is a legislative function, and a hearing is not a prerequisite [***2] unless the Legislature so directs, which it failed to do in the instant legislation. There is a reasonable basis for the respondent's determination that an application of the regulation will result in rate schedules reasonably related to the costs of efficient production of hospital services, and, therefore, his determination should not be disturbed. Furthermore, there has been no violation of the supremacy clause of the United States Constitution.

2. Respondent's denial, without a hearing, of each petitioner hospital's application for a waiver of the section was improper. Such action is judicial in nature and, under the circumstances, due process requires each petitioner be given an opportunity to be heard and present evidence to establish that a waiver was warranted. Furthermore, the denial on the conclusory statement that granting the waiver was "not found to be a matter of public interest and necessity" was improper. Finally, since a denial could not be predicated on grounds unrelated to cost efficiency, it was improper to deny the application of a waiver because of alleged operational and structural deficiencies based on the "Life Safety Code".

 

1266 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dordal


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


55 A.D.2d 787; 390 N.Y.S.2d 15; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 15579



December 23, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the County Court of Albany County (New York), which convicted defendant of burglary in the third degree, and sentenced defendant, as a second felony offender, to a term of imprisonment with a maximum of four years and a minimum of two years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that he was erroneously sentenced as a second felony offender because there was insufficient proof that he had a prior felony conviction. On appeal, the court disagreed and affirmed the conviction and sentence. To qualify as a predicate felony under N.Y. Penal Law § 70.06(1)(b)(i), an out-of-state conviction had to be of an offense for which a sentence to prison term in excess of one year or a sentence of death was authorized, and could be authorized in New York, irrespective of whether such a sentence was imposed. The evidence clearly established that defendant was previously convicted of second degree robbery in California, and that a sentence in excess of one year was authorized for that crime. In addition, a sentence in excess of one year was authorized for a comparable crime by N.Y. Penal Law § 160.05. As such, the prerequisites of N.Y. Penal Law § 70.06(1)(b)(i) had been established, and defendant was properly adjudged to be a second felony offender. Defendant's final claim that § 70.06 was unconstitutional failed because his identical argument had previously been rejected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting and sentencing defendant.

 

1267 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Comiskey v. Arlen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


55 A.D.2d 304; 390 N.Y.S.2d 122; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14566



December 20, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Order insofar as appealed from reversed, without costs or disbursements, and the said branches of plaintiffs' motion are denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, doctor and hospital, and intervenor attorney general challenged so much of an order of the Supreme Court (New York), as declared N.Y. Jud. Law § 148-a unconstitutional and suppressed the recommendation of the medical malpractice panel finding no liability on the part of defendants, in a medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff patient brought a medical malpractice action against defendants. Pursuant to N.Y. Jud. Law § 148-a, the case was heard before a medical malpractice mediation panel after the completion of discovery. The panel determined there was no malpractice and plaintiff moved to have the panel's recommendation suppressed. The trial court held that § 148-a was unconstitutional and ruled that the recommendation could not be introduced at trial. Defendants and the attorney general challenged the order and the court reversed. The court held that the trial court's assumption that no jury could evaluate a medical malpractice panel's recommendation with objectivity was unwarranted and could not serve as the basis for a declaration of unconstitutionality. The court noted that under § 148-a, the jury remained the ultimate arbiter of the factual questions raised at the trial and concluded that the statute constituted a legislative exception to the hearsay rule.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order finding the statute requiring submission of medical malpractice cases to a medical malpractice mediation panel unconstitutional. The court held that the statute was constitutional and that the recommendation of the panel should not have been suppressed.


HEADNOTES

Physicians and surgeons -- malpractice -- medical mediation panel -- constitutionality.

1. Subdivision 8 of section 148-a of the Judiciary Law, which provides that if the three members of a medical malpractice panel concur, their written recommendation shall be admissible in evidence at a trial and shall not be binding on the jury or trial court but shall be accorded such weight as the jury or court chooses, is constitutional. The statute does not infringe on the right to a trial by jury. The jury remains the ultimate arbiter of the factual questions raised at a trial. The panel's recommendation is an expert opinion to be evaluated by the jury. Under these [***2] circumstances, the Legislature has amended the hearsay rule of evidence, which is within its power to do. The determination of the panel must be unanimous to be admissible, and it can never be the sole basis for entry of a judgment.

2. The statute is not violative of due process by denying a right of access to the courts. The right of access to the courts will be accorded constitutional protection only where the right sought to be asserted is a right recognized in a constitutional sense as carrying a preferred status and so entitled to special protection.

3. The statute does not violate the equal protection clause. The classification in the statute has a rational basis and must be upheld.

People v. Kapp


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


55 A.D.2d 779; 389 N.Y.S.2d 645; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 15568
