1269 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Tierney v. State


Claim Nos. 54620, 54621


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


55 A.D.2d 158; 389 N.Y.S.2d 709; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14075



December 17, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Order unanimously reversed, without costs and motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the judgment of the Court of Claims (New York), which denied the state's motion to consolidate respondent husband's wrongful death claim, filed on behalf of his deceased wife's estate, and the husband's personal injury claim, and which denied the state's motion for leave to file and serve a contribution counterclaim against the husband individually.


OVERVIEW: The husband and his wife were in a car accident on a state road and his wife was fatally injured. Alleging state's negligence in the design, construction, or maintenance of the state road, the husband filed a claim against the state for personal injuries, and also filed a claim against the state, on behalf of his wife's estate, for wrongful death. The state requested that the trial court consolidate the claims and allow it to file a contribution counterclaim against the husband. The trial court denied the state's requests, stating that it was bound by precedent. The state appealed and argued that it would be in the best interest of justice, including promotion of judicial economy, to allow the consolidation and counterclaim, and argued that the precedent could be overruled or distinguished. The court held that the precedent was overruled to the extent it precluded a counterclaim in such a case. By commencing a suit in a court of claims, the husband impliedly consented to the interposition by the state of a counterclaim which the trial court could entertain, at least where the counterclaim arose out of the same or similar transactions that gave rise to the husband's cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of the state's motion for leave to file and serve a contribution counterclaim against the husband individually, and granted the state's petition.


HEADNOTES

State -- Court of Claims -- counterclaim for apportionment of liability.

1. Claims against the State for damages arising out of an automobile accident which resulted in injuries to claimant operator and the death of his wife, a passenger, were filed by the driver individually and as administrator of the estate of his wife, alleging that the accident was caused by the State's negligence in the design, construction and/or maintenance of the highway. The Court of Claims has jurisdiction to entertain a counterclaim for apportionment or indemnity filed by the State against the driver for any recovery had against the State upon the claim by the passenger's estate. By filing a claim against the State in the Court of Claims, claimant driver waived his right to a jury trial of any counterclaim which the State may have against him. Moreover, the counterclaim [***2] should be allowed in the interest of judicial economy. ( Bartlett v State of New York, 40 AD2d 267, overruled in part.)

2. The counterclaim is deemed timely, although not served within 20 days after service of the claims, as contemplated by rule 14 of the Rules of the Court of Claims (22 NYCRR 1200.15).

 

1270 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Board of Education v. Pisa


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


55 A.D.2d 128; 389 N.Y.S.2d 938; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14555; 94 L.R.R.M. 2556



December 17, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Orders and judgment affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teachers union and its president (collectively union) sought review of a judgment which enjoined the union from striking and which imposed sanctions for criminal contempt for willfully violating a temporary restraining order (TRO) and the preliminary injunction obtained by respondent board of education (board).


OVERVIEW: The union argued that N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 211 operated to deprive public employees' equal protection of the law and that its application was unconstitutional. The union also argued that the TRO and preliminary injunction were invalid. The court held that the union failed to provide sufficient evidence to rebut the strong presumption of the constitutionality of § 211. The court held that the TRO was valid and was necessary as evidenced by the fact that the union had threatened to strike, which would have caused irreparable harm. The court further noted that § 211 allowed a TRO to issue based only on a threat of a strike. The court found that the trial court did not err when it issued the preliminary injunction, because the record revealed that at the time the injunction was issued, the union contrary to the TRO, was on strike. The court held that the union was not denied a right to a fair trial during the second contempt proceeding, after the first had been reversed, because there was no evidence that the judge was prejudicial or biased and the fact that the trial judge found them again guilty of contempt and imposed the same sentence did not prove bias.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which imposed criminal contempt penalties and a preliminary injunction upon the union.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- Public Employees' Fair Employment Act -- illegal strikes.

1. The lack of statutory power of the Public Employment Relations Board to enforce its decisions directing negotiations between public employers and employees by compelling specific performance of negotiated agreements has not been shown to create any imbalance denying public employees equal protection of the law in view of the statutory prohibition against employee strikes, since no proof has been presented that public employers and employees are in the same class for purposes of the Fourteenth Amendment.

2. Absent proof that public employers and employees are in the same legislative classification, no constitutional question is [***2] presented by denial of any right of school employees to negotiate directly with the city, although the board of education is bound in fixing wages and salaries by the budget allocated by the city.

3. Section 204-a of the Civil Service Law, providing that public employment collective bargaining agreements contain a notice that provisions requiring legislation or additional funds are subject to legislative approval, explicitly recognizes that the public employer's authority to enter a contract is subject to the appropriation of funds. Accordingly, the public employees' statutory right to negotiate may properly be altered by legislative enactment.

4. A temporary restraining order prohibiting defendants from engaging in a strike was sufficiently supported by allegations that a strike was threatened, and any lack of factual allegations of irreparable harm is not fatal, since a strike of public employees by its nature causes irreparable harm.

5. Since public employees were on strike in violation of section 210 of the Civil Service Law a preliminary injunction was properly issued.

6. Although orders enjoining defendants from engaging in various strike activities would be subject to modification [***3] to the extent that they exceeded the prohibitions specified in section 210 of the Civil Service Law, the issue is moot, since the strike has ended.

7. Notwithstanding overbroadness of the injunction, the orders were not void upon their faces, had to be obeyed and may properly be the basis for a conviction of criminal contempt.

8. The holding of a second contempt proceeding before the same Justice who presided over the first hearing, after the first was overturned for lack of personal jurisdiction, did not deprive defendants of a fair trial. There was no claim of prejudice on the first trial, and a mere showing of prior judicial exposure to the parties or questions does not require disqualification of a Justice. Actual bias does not necessitate reversal unless the Justice's decision is based thereon, and no such bias may be found from the fact that the Justice had previously found the defendants guilty and that he employed similar language in his two decisions on the matter.

9. The finding that the defendant president of a public employee union was guilty of criminal contempt was adequately supported by evidence that he failed to take action to rescind strike recommendations and [***4] that he stated that he would not do so until union demands were negotiated.

10. A 30-day sentence of imprisonment and a $ 250 fine against the individual defendant were within the limits provided by section 751 of the Judiciary Law, and absent a clear abuse of discretion the imposition of such sentence should not be reversed.

11. Section 751 of the Judiciary Law (subd 2, par [a]) allows the court, in fixing contempt punishment, discretion as to consideration of acts of extreme provocation by the public employer, and, absent a clear abuse of discretion there may be no review of the sufficiency of the consideration given to that factor.

12. In fixing the sentence for contempt, the court properly evaluated the impact of the strike upon the public health, safety and welfare, finding that school children were deprived of the services of union members as a result of the defendants' illegal actions.

13. Although less than half of the union dues collected were retained for local use, rather than the two thirds found by the court, there was no abuse of discretion in setting the fine against the defendant union.

 

1271 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Keystone Associates v. State


Claim No. 49592


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


55 A.D.2d 85; 389 N.Y.S.2d 895; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14547



December 16, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, on the law and the facts, without costs, and matter remitted to the Court of Claims with direction to take such further proceedings as it may deem appropriate and thereupon to award damages in the amount of all carrying costs and maintenance costs during the period of the easement less whatever sum the claimant received from the security deposit provided by chapter 691 of the Laws of 1966.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent state sought review of the decision from the Court of Claims (New York), which granted damages and attorney fees to claimant property owner for a taking caused by a temporary easement created when the legislature attempted to take the property owner's land through a statutory condemnation proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The legislature passed a bill that delayed the issuance of a demolition permit to the property owners and permitted the state to take the property owner's land through condemnation proceedings. The property owner successfully challenged the constitutionality of the law and thereafter made a claim for the temporary taking of its property. The trial court awarded damages for lost rental profits and also awarded attorney fees for the legal fees and expenses incurred in the course of having the statute declared unconstitutional. The state challenged the decision and the court reversed and remanded. The property owners were only entitled, by virtue of the temporary easement, to receive as damages all carrying and maintenance costs during the period of the easement. Any damages for the increased construction costs caused by the delay in construction would have been offset by increased rents due to the same inflation. Additionally, the award of attorney fees was inappropriate because the fees were associated with a prior action and the property owner was not entitled to the reimbursement of its legal expenses associated with vindicating its rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the award of damages and attorney fees in favor of the property owner and remanded for a determination of the carrying and maintenance costs associated with the state's temporary easement.


HEADNOTES

Eminent domain -- compensation -- temporary appropriation.

1. After it was established that a taking resulted from the eight-month delay in issuing claimant a permit to demolish the old Metropolitan Opera House pursuant to the terms of a lease, which situation resulted from an unconstitutional statute authorizing the withholding of the demolition permit upon the deposit of $ 200,000 as security pending action of a corporation newly created for the purpose of acquiring and preserving the "Old Met" by condemnation proceedings (L 1966, ch 691), damages were awarded for [***2] the temporary appropriation of claimant's interest. The Court of Claims erred in awarding lost profit and increased construction costs, there being nothing but speculation as to any damage to the claimant when considered as a temporary, total easement. The present action presents an ad hoc situation in which the Legislature attempted to provide just compensation for the withholding of a demolition permit and the situation is such as to require an exception to the general rule of damages for loss of rental value. Accordingly, the existence of a temporary easement requires that the claimant receive as damages all carrying and maintenance costs during the period of the easement. Except for such costs, the claimant failed to establish any damages.

2. It was error to award claimant legal fees and expenses incurred in litigating the constitutionality of chapter 691 of the Laws of 1966.

 

1272 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Juan R. v. Necta V.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


55 A.D.2d 33; 389 N.Y.S.2d 126; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14536



December 13, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Order of the Family Court, Kings County, dated October 21, 1975, affirmed, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a visitation action filed by respondent putative father, appellant natural mother sought review of a decision from the Family Court, Kings County (New York), which denied her motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Putative father sought visitation of children he claimed to have had with the natural mother. The mother denied the father's paternity and filed a motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction pursuant to N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 651. The trial court denied the motion. The mother sought review and argued that that "custody" as used in the statute did not include "visitation" and that the family court lacked jurisdiction under the statute to entertain a petition for visitation. The court affirmed. It found that "custody" as used in N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 651 did not exclude "visitation" and did not require dismissal of the petition. It found that visitation was a form of limited custody and it was well-established that the standard of adjudication in either instance was the "best interests" of the child. Therefore, the greater term "custody" encompassed the lesser term "visitation".


OUTCOME: The court found that the trial court had jurisdiction to hear visitation matters and affirmed the denial of the mother's motion to dismiss.


HEADNOTES

Parent and child -- visitation rights -- jurisdiction of Family Court.

1. The term "custody" as used in subdivision (b) of section 651 of the Family Court Act, which states that, when initiated in the Family Court, that court has jurisdiction of a proceeding to determine custody of minors, does not exclude "visitation" rights. "Visitation" is a form of limited custody and the standard of adjudication in either instance is the best interests of the children. Accordingly, the greater term "custody" encompasses the lesser term "visitation" and a proceeding by a putative father against the natural mother to secure rights of visitation with his illegitimate children was properly brought in the Family Court.

2. Moreover, implicit in the constitutional right of the Family Court to determine "custody" (NY Const, art VI, § 13 ) must be the right [***2] to determine "visitation".

 

1273 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


McNamara v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


54 A.D.2d 467; 389 N.Y.S.2d 682; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14066



December 10, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously reversed, on the law with costs, and matter remitted to Board of Education, City School District, City of Rochester for proceedings in accordance with opinion by Goldman, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner teachers appealed a decision of the Supreme Court at Special Term in Monroe County (New York), which dismissed their petition for reinstatement in an action against respondent Board of Education of City School District of City of Rochester that involved tenure issues.


OVERVIEW: The teachers worked for the school district in the pre-kindergarten area. Federal funding was reduced and the board abolished their positions and terminated them on the ground that they had the least seniority in terms of continuous years of service than the other teachers in their area. The teachers brought an action for reinstatement, but the trial court dismissed their petition. The teachers appealed, arguing, inter alia, that the pre-kindergarten tenure was part of the kindergarten area and that meant that they had seniority over some of the kindergarten teachers. The court reversed and remitted to the board, holding that pre-kindergarten was included in the elementary tenure area, and the board was required to determine the teachers' seniority by a comparison with all elementary teachers. The court held that if the teachers were not the least senior elementary teachers, they were to be reinstated with back pay, benefits, and privileges.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remitted a judgment that dismissed the teachers' petition in an action resulting from a board decision terminating the teachers because they were in a separate tenure area than other elementary teachers and that had less seniority in their tenure area.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- teachers -- tenure areas -- pre-kindergarten teachers.

1. In the absence of reported decisions regarding the status of pre-kindergarten teachers with respect to tenure areas, any evidence of historical custom or practice which would shed light on the question, or any compelling authority on either side of the question, it is held that pre-kindergarten teachers are included in the elementary tenure area even if they were appointed prior to August 1, 1975, the effective date of a rule of the Board of Regents which provides that "Kindergarten (including pre-kindergarten programs) together with the first six grades shall constitute the elementary tenure area" (8 NYCRR 30.4). Accordingly, a judgment of Special Term, which dismissed [***2] a petition in a proceeding for reinstatement brought by teachers who had taught in a nursery school project which was Federally funded, and whose positions were abolished due to a reduction in that funding, is reversed, and the matter is remitted to the board of education of their city school district for a determination of their seniority by a comparison with all teachers in the elementary tenure area, and, in the event they are not the least senior teachers in that tenure area, for their reinstatement.

2. Joinder of allegedly less senior teachers as parties to petitioners' proceeding would have been premature, since the board acted in a mistaken belief as to which tenure area petitioners occupied, and never determined their relative seniority within the elementary tenure area. The prescribed standards for determining seniority can become complicated, and the orderly and desirable way to proceed is to have the board make the determination initially. Once it identifies those teachers it deems least senior, they, if so advised, may seek judicial review and join those whom they seek to oust.

 

1274 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Sloma v. Hynes


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


54 A.D.2d 493; 389 N.Y.S.2d 670; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14070



December 10, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner nursing home owner (owner) sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court of Erie County (New York) that denied a motion by the owner to quash a subpoena issued by respondent special prosecutor in a nursing home investigation.


OVERVIEW: The special prosecutor who was conducting an investigation subpoenaed the owner to present certain information pertaining to his business. The owner filed a motion to quash the subpoena arguing that the subpoena issued by the special prosecution under N.Y. Exec. Law § 63(8) violated his right to due process of law. Specifically, the owner contended that § 63(8) was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed the supreme court's judgment denying the owner's motion to quash because no authority was presented for declaring § 63(8) unconstitutional due to the undefined breadth and scope of the investigatory powers conferred on the special prosecutor. The court found that if credence was given to the owner's challenge, the legislature would have to authorize every criminal investigation by the attorney general's office no matter how narrow, germane, and infused with the public interest the desired investigation might be. The court concluded that the holding did not appear constitutionally required or administratively reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the supreme court that denied the owner's motion to quash a subpoena issued by the special prosecutor in an investigation of the owner's nursing home.


HEADNOTES

Witnesses -- subpoena -- constitutionality of subdivision 8 of section 63 of Executive Law.

Subdivision 8 of section 63 of the Executive Law, which provides that the Attorney-General may, with the approval of the Governor and when directed by the Governor, inquire into matters concerning the public peace, safety and justice and is empowered to subpoena witnesses, is not violative of due process of law for vagueness. If credence were given to the constitutional challenge, the Legislature would have to authorize every criminal investigation by the Attorney-General's office no matter how narrow, germane and infused with the public interest the investigation might be, and such a holding does not appear to be constitutionally required or administratively reasonable. Accordingly, a motion to quash a subpoena issued by the office of the Special State Prosecutor in a nursing home investigation was properly denied.

 

1275 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Bookhout v. Levitt


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


54 A.D.2d 477; 389 N.Y.S.2d 164; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14067



December 9, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Determination modified, by annulling that portion thereof denying petitioners' additional retirement service credit for accumulated unused sick leave at the time of retirement, and matter remitted for a recomputation of petitioners' retirement allowances, and, as so modified, confirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner retirees instituted a N.Y.C.P.L.R. 78 proceeding to review a determination of respondent state comptroller, which denied their applications for a redetermination of their retirement allowances.


OVERVIEW: The retirees were all members of the New York State Employees' Retirement System and they included former surrogate's court, county court and family court judges, a former county treasurer and a former county clerk. In each instance, the state comptroller determined, pursuant to the procedures of N.Y. Retire & Soc. Sec. Law § 74, that lump-sum payments for accumulated unused vacation time and additional service credits for accumulated unused sick leave would not be included in the computation of the retirees' retirement allowances. The court held that the retirees who were elected public officials did not have a vested or contractual right in their unused vacation time and were therefore not entitled to a retirement credit for that time. However, the court held that the retirees, who were elected or not elected, had a vested right in their unused sick leave pursuant to N.Y. Retire & Soc. Sec. Law § 33, 41. Therefore the court modified the state comptroller's determination, by annulling the state comptroller's denial of the retirees' additional retirement service credit for accumulated unused sick leave at the time of retirement.


OUTCOME: The court modified the state comptroller's determination, by annulling the state comptroller's denial of the retirees' additional retirement service credit for accumulated unused sick leave at the time of retirement in the retirees' action which challenged the state comptroller's decision with respect to the retirement benefits.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- retirement and pension benefits -- elected public officials -- lump sum payments for accumulated unused vacation time -- retirement service credit for accumulated unused sick leave.

1. In computing the retirement allowances of elected county officials, lump sum payments for accumulated unused vacation time, which were authorized by their county, are not includible. Such payments are to be excluded from the computation under section 431 of the Retirement and Social Security Law, and, while it has been [***2] judicially determined that that section was unconstitutional if applied to public employees who were members of the Retirement System before the date of its enactment, the basis of that decision was that such members had acquired a vested right to the benefit arising from an established pattern of prior administrative practice. Elected public officials have not acquired such a vested right since, with respect to them, the Comptroller has consistently followed a policy of disallowing retirement credit for such payments, stating, in an opinion, that he considered such payments made to elected officials to be highly irregular, improper and probably illegal.

2. However, elected county officials are entitled to additional retirement service credit for accumulated unused sick leave, a benefit which their county elected to extend to them. There is specific statutory basis for the inclusion of such leave ( Retirement and Social Security Law, §§ 33, 41), with no distinction made between elected and nonelected employees or members, in sharp contrast to the statutory prohibition against the inclusion of lump sum payments for accumulated unused vacation time.

 

1276 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Rotodyne, Inc. v. Consolidated Edison Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


55 A.D.2d 600; 389 N.Y.S.2d 387; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 15307



December 6, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, on the law, with $ 50 costs and disbursements, and motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action, inter alia, to foreclose a mechanic's lien, defendant corporation appealed from an order of the Supreme Court, Westchester County (New York) that denied its motion for partial summary judgment dismissing the first cause of action for foreclosure of the mechanic's lien, and to vacate the lien.


OVERVIEW: In an action to foreclose a mechanic's lien, the trial court denied the corporation's motion for partial summary judgment dismissing the first cause of action for foreclosure of the mechanic's lien, and to vacate the lien. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court decision and granted the motion. The court found that at the time the contract was entered into, N.Y. Lien Law § 34 permitted the written waiver of a mechanic's lien. However, effective July 1, 1975, former § 34 was repealed and a new § 34 was added, which section provided that any contract, agreement, or understanding whereby the right to file or enforce any lien created under article two was waived, was void as against public policy and wholly unenforceable. The court found that the legislature intended the statute to apply only to those contracts entered into after its effective date. The court found that the contract in question was entered into in reliance upon the law as it then existed, and the parties regulated their conduct accordingly.


OUTCOME: In an action to foreclose a mechanic's lien, the court reversed an order of the trial court that denied the corporation's motion for partial summary judgment dismissing the first cause of action for foreclosure of the mechanic's lien, and to vacate the lien. The court granted the motion.

Balmer v. New York State Board of Parole


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


54 A.D.2d 979; 388 N.Y.S.2d 929; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14927

1278 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


McBride v. Forestburgh


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


54 A.D.2d 396; 388 N.Y.S.2d 940; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14053



November 24, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court, Sullivan County (New York), which declared certain zoning ordinances of defendant town valid and constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The landowners presented a preliminary plot plan for the development of a mobile home park to the town when there were no regulations governing the submission of subdivision plans to the planning board and no zoning ordinances concerning subdivisions or mobile home parks. After the town enacted ordinances requiring a one-acre lot for conventional and mobile homes. The landowners sought a judgment declaring the various ordinances unconstitutional and ineffective to prevent them from using their property for any use permitted when they presented their plan. The court affirmed the trial court's declaration that the ordinances were constitutional. The statutory requirements of N.Y. Town Law § 263 were met because implicit in the ordinances was the element of planning that was rational and consistent with basic land use policies of the community. The town made a sufficient showing that there was some rational planning prior to adoption of the ordinance and the ordinance was consistent with the community's development policies. The landowners did not have any vested rights prior to adoption of the ordinance and failed to demonstrate the other permitted uses were not feasible.


OUTCOME: The judgment declaring the challenged zoning ordinance constitutional was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- constitutionality of ordinances.

1. Plaintiffs had presented to the Town Board of the Town of Forestburgh and the Town Planning Board a preliminary plot plan for the development of a mobile home park before rules or regulations existed for the submission of plans to the Planning Board and before there were any zoning ordinances in the town concerning subdivisions or mobile home parks. As applied to plaintiffs' property, subsequently enacted ordinances, i.e., a house trailer ordinance, a subdivision ordinance and a comprehensive zoning ordinance superseding the first two which required a minimum one-acre lot, are constitutional.

2. The zoning ordinance is not ultra vires. There was a sufficient showing of a comprehensive plan which was rational and consistent with the basic land use policies of the sparsely populated town which is rural and rustic [***2] in character.

3. While the proof may have established that plaintiffs would suffer significant economic injury if the ordinances were enforced, a showing that the town was concerned with preserving its rural and rustic nature and that the character of the community would be adversely affected by the proposed development shifted the burden to plaintiffs to establish that the ordinance amounted to a taking and this they failed to do. Furthermore, they failed to meet the burden of overcoming the presumption of constitutionality. Consequently, the ordinance is not confiscatory as applied to plaintiffs' property.

4. Expenditures for an evironmental impact study and other preliminary inspections did not vest any rights in plaintiffs. Lack of actual construction, coupled with the notice plaintiffs had that a one-acre minimum for subdivisions was under consideration, compels the conclusion that they failed to establish a vested interest.

 

1279 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Phelan v. Buffalo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


54 A.D.2d 262; 388 N.Y.S.2d 469; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13765



November 12, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of the judgment of the Supreme Court (New York) granting declaratory judgment to plaintiff voter and declaring that the city's local law establishing a durational residency requirement for eligibility to hold office was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted a law that no person would be eligible for election to enumerated offices who had not been a domiciled resident of the city for a period of at least two years preceding the date of the election. The voter, who did not meet the residency requirement, filed an action seeking a declaration that the law was unconstitutional and void. The trial court declared the law unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the residency restriction invidiously discriminated against the voter and others and violated the Equal Protection and Due Process Clauses of the state and United States Constitutions. The city failed to meet its burden to show that the limitation upon candidates and voters was essential to serve a compelling state interest. It served no necessary governmental objective for the city to declare that a two-year city resident had a greater familiarity with and a greater stake in the problems, conditions, needs, and life of his community than a more recent resident.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court declaring that the city's local law establishing a two-year residence requirement for eligibility to hold enumerated offices was unconstitutional, in the declaratory judgment action brought by the voter.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- durational residency requirement for public office.

1. Local Law No. 1 of the Local Laws of 1975 of the City of Buffalo, effective January 7, 1975, which provides that "No person shall be eligible for election or appointment as a successor to the office of mayor, comptroller, president of the council or councilman-at-large who has not been a domiciled resident of the city for a period of at least two (2) years preceding the date of his election or appointment", is unconstitutional as violative of the equal protection and due process clauses of both the Federal and the State Constitutions. The residency restrictions imposed by it invidiously discriminate against the candidates impeded thereby and the voters who wish to support them, and there has been no demonstration of any compelling governmental need for the imposition of such restrictions.

2. A resident of the city since June, 1974,  [***2] who was an unsuccessful candidate for the office of President of the Common Council in the 1974 general election, when there was no durational residency requirement for eligibility to hold any of the offices enumerated in the local law, and who was an alleged intended candidate for the office of councilman-at-large in the 1975 general election, had standing to bring the present action for a declaration that the local law was unconstitutional. Having qualified as a candidate in the past, he had a legally protected interest which was adversely affected in a real and immediate manner by its promulgation. Additionally, his status as a qualified voter in the city gives him standing to complain of a claimed unconstitutional encroachment upon his right to vote.

3. Although the issue is academic and moot as to this plaintiff's candidacy, since he never became a candidate for city-wide office in 1975 despite the trial court's declaration that the local law was unconstitutional, nor, apparently, did he attempt to do so, the controversy is of public importance and of a character likely to recur with respect to others, warranting a determination of the issues raised.

 

1280 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Tucker v. Toia


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


54 A.D.2d 322; 388 N.Y.S.2d 475; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14035



November 12, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Order unanimously affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff home relief benefit recipients obtained a preliminary injunction in the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), preventing defendant Commissioner of the New York State Department of Social Services from implementing 1976 N.Y. Laws ch. 76, § 15, amending N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 158(a). The Commissioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The benefit recipients argued that the statute, affecting eligibility for home relief, violated the New York Constitution. The court held that although the argument might not ultimately have been successful, it was based on substantial principles of constitutional law and involved novel issues of first impression. The question of the statute's validity involved aspects of constitutional law too weighty to have been briefed adequately in the short time available to the parties before the motion was heard in the trial court and too complex for the trial court to resolve in the even shorter time available to it before its decision was required. In view of the conceded irreparable harm facing the benefit recipients, contrasted with the damage the state would face by postponing implementation of the statute until the case could be heard on its merits, a preliminary injunction was appropriate. It was error for the trial court to have orally declared the statute unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, without costs, the issuance of the preliminary injunction.


HEADNOTES

Social services -- home relief -- eligibility of persons under 21 years of age.

1. Plaintiffs were about to have their home relief benefits terminated as a result of a proposed implementation of section 15 of chapter 76 of the Laws of 1976, which amended section 158 (subd [a]) of the Social Services Law to provide that no person under 21 years of age except a married person living with their spouse, living apart from a legally responsible relative shall be eligible for home relief unless a proceeding has been brought by or on behalf of such person to compel the legally responsible relative to provide for or contribute to such person's support and until an order of disposition has been entered in such proceeding. In an action by them for judgment declaring the amendment unconstitutional, wherein their right to ultimate relief is predicated upon an argument that the amendment is violative of important [***2] principles contained in the New York Constitution, they moved for a preliminary injunction against the implementation of the amendment pending a final resolution of the merits of their action. Special Term properly exercised its discretion in granting their motion. They would suffer irreparable injury if the preliminary injunction was not granted, in contrast to the damage the State would face by postponing implementation of the statute until the case can be heard on the merits, and, while their argument may not prove to be ultimately successful, it is based on substantial principles of constitutional law and involves novel issues of first impression, too weighty to have been briefed adequately in the short time available to the parties before the motion was heard at Special Term and too complex for Special Term to resolve in the even shorter time available to it before its decision was required. This is precisely the situation in which a preliminary injunction should be granted to hold the parties in status quo while the legal issues are determined in a deliberate and judicious manner.

2. A decision of a Federal court, upholding the amendment against a challenge based solely [***3] upon the Federal Constitution's guarantees of due process and equal protection, is not controlling.

3. While Special Term properly granted the preliminary injunction, it erred when, at the hearing on the motion, it seemingly determined the merits by orally declaring that the amendment was unconstitutional. However, it did not repeat this finding of unconstitutionality in the order which it rendered.

 

1281 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Strongin v. Nyquist


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


54 A.D.2d 1031; 388 N.Y.S.2d 683; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14992



November 10, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Judgment modified, on the law and the facts, by annulling so much of the determination as found petitioner guilty of charge II and by reducing the penalty to a suspension of six months without pay, and, as so modified, affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a tenured teacher, challenged an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term in Albany County (New York), which dismissed her N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 application to vacate and set aside a decision of respondents, the Commissioner of Education and the Board of Education, which terminated her services.


OVERVIEW: Respondents terminated the tenured teacher's services even though a panel conducted a hearing pursuant to N.Y, Educ. Law § 3020-a and found her not guilty of the charges. The teacher's N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding was dismissed and the teacher sought review. The court modified the decision and affirmed, finding that (1) N.Y. Educ. Law § 3020-a was not violated because the Board sufficiently stated the reasons relied upon for the determination; (2) there was no evidence that the Board had a pecuniary interest in the matter that resulted in bias against the teacher, and there was no due process violation due to the combined decision making and investigatory powers in the Board; (3) there was substantial evidence to support the Board's findings as to the charges of inefficiency and incompetency, but the finding that the teacher committed the minor transgressions failed to support the Board's determination that she was guilty of the charges of insubordination, neglect of duty, and conduct unbecoming a teacher. Because the second charge was not supported by the record, the Commissioner's action as to that charge was arbitrary and the penalty imposed had to be reassessed.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of dismissal by annulling so much of the determination as found the teacher guilty of the second charge and by reducing the penalty to a suspension of six months without pay.

Voss v. Voss


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


54 A.D.2d 1032; 388 N.Y.S.2d 182; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14993



November 10, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-husband challenged an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term in Albany County (New York), which denied his motion to vacate the provisions for the respondent ex-wife's support and maintenance that were incorporated in the judgment of divorce.


OVERVIEW: The ex-husband obtained an absolute divorce against the ex-wife on the grounds of cruel and inhuman treatment. A default judgment was entered that awarded support and maintenance to the ex-wife, of which only a few payments were made. The ex-wife brought an action in family court to collect the arrearages and to modify the support order. The ex-husband moved to vacate the support order and to stay the proceedings on grounds that N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law §§ 236, 244 and 245, and Fam. Ct. Act § 412, were unconstitutional. The court affirmed the order, finding that the ex-husband did not have standing to attack the constitutionality of the statutes. The court found that (1) the ex-husband waived his right under N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 236 to negate his obligation to pay support when the divorce was based on the ex-wife's misconduct because his agreement to pay was given in exchange for the ex-wife's agreement to an uncontested divorce; (2) the ex-wife relied on the agreement and waiver; (3) the ex-husband could not be relieved of the support obligation he assumed; and (4) the support obligation was not based on Fam. Ct. Act § 412, which only applied before a decree was entered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

1283 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Dykeman v. Symonds


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


54 A.D.2d 159; 388 N.Y.S.2d 422; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13744



November 5, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizen instituted a proceeding to determine whether respondent public official, who occupied the offices of county legislator and motor vehicle supervisor, held incompatible offices and had violated N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 801. The Supreme Court at Special Term, Yates County (New York) held that the offices were incompatible and granted the citizen's summary judgment motion, and the public official appealed.


OVERVIEW: A motor vehicle supervisor was elected to the county legislature and continued to hold her supervisor's office but refrained from voting on matters affecting her salary. She claimed that a citizen lacked standing to bring suit, that her right to hold office could only be tested in an action quo warranto, and that requiring her to vacate her office disenfranchised the voters in her district. The court held that the official had violated § 801 and must resign from one office. As a taxpayer and county resident the citizen had standing to challenge dual office holding under a statute enacted for the community's benefit. A quo warranto proceeding was not the exclusive remedy where the issue was one of law and no factual determinations were required. The county legislature set the motor vehicle supervisor's salary and it was immaterial whether the official refrained from voting on salary matters because the possibility of wrongdoing prohibited the holding of incompatible offices. The statute was not unconstitutional and did not arbitrarily exclude the official from office because there was a rational basis for the public policy stated in § 801 forbidding conflicts of interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in the citizen's favor.


HEADNOTES

Public officers -- dual employment.

1. Respondent may not serve in the position of County Legislator to which she was elected and continue to hold her prior appointive position as County Motor Vehicle Supervisor, for which her salary is fixed by the County Legislature, since section 801 of the General Municipal Law provides that municipal officers may not have an interest in any municipal contract for which they have a duty to negotiate, prepare, authorize or approve the contract or payment thereunder. The statutory purpose is to avoid the possibility of breach of trust and, accordingly, the acceptance of an office implies resignation of a prior incompatible office.

2. Although quo warranto is generally the remedy available to try title to an office, mandamus is proper where,  [***2] as here, the issue is solely one of law.

3. Since there is no question of fact, summary judgment is appropriate.

4. Petitioner, as a county resident and taxpayer, has standing to bring a proceeding based upon a violation of section 801 of the General Municipal Law, since the statute was enacted for the benefit of the community in general.

5. The requirement that respondent resign from one of her two offices does not unconstitutionally disenfranchise the voters of her district, since respondent may, by resignation from her appointive office, serve in the elective office, and the requirement has a reasonable basis.

 

1284 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Montoroula v. Parry


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


54 A.D.2d 327; 388 N.Y.S.2d 916; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14036



November 1, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state commissioner challenged the order of the Supreme Court of Orange County (New York), which declared N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 365(2) and N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 18, § 360.21(e) unconstitutional and remitted the application filed by appellee father for financial assistance for psychiatric treatment for his son.


OVERVIEW: The father's son suffered from severe mental and psychiatric problems, although he had never been declared judicially incompetent. The father applied for medical assistance under the Social Services Law in placing his son in a private institution. The county commissioner denied the application, and the state commissioner confirmed the decision. The father argued that his adult child had been deprived of the equal protection of the laws because the statute and the regulation unlawfully discriminated in their classifications, based upon age and the kind of illness described. The court reversed the trial court's order because neither the statute nor the regulation violated the requirements of the equal protection of the laws. The court applied the rational basis standard and determined that the statute and regulation did not offend the equal protection of the laws. The court took into account the circumstances surrounding the status of the young and elderly in the community and the nature of the treatment a mental illness involved.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court that declared provisions of the Social Services Law unconstitutional was reversed, and the father's action was dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Social services -- Medicaid.

1. Subdivision 2 of section 365 of the Social Services Law and 18 NYCRR 360.21 (e), which provide for medical assistance to eligible persons under 21 years of age or 65 years of age and over who are receiving in-patient psychiatric services, are constitutional and are not violative of equal protection. The subdivision and the regulation are part of the State plan implementing the Federal Medicaid program. In determining to whom assistance is to be provided, the subdivision and regulation establish classifications based upon a person's age and type of disability. As a result of these classifications, assistance [***2] is not provided for in-patient services in private hospitals for persons suffering from mental disabilities who are over 21 years of age and under 65. Traditionally, the young and the old have been objects of the community's solicitude and classification by age has been a conventional legislative method for marking the area of statutory application. Since age limitations may appear arbitrary from one view, yet rational from another, the matter of determining the age limitations is left to the legislative judgment, which must be afforded the preference in our system of government.

2. The Legislature may also choose to limit benefits on the basis of the type of disability and, within a type, may limit assistance to those persons in public institutions. The rational basis supporting these limitations may be the experimental nature of the program or budgetary restrictions. Classifications in the law need not be perfect to be constitutional. The Legislature cannot be faulted for addressing itself to only one phase of a problem or for failing to treat all afflictions equally. Choices must and will be made and priorities must and will be set. Accordingly, plaintiff's application for [***3] medical assistance in placing his 24-year-old mentally disabled son in a private institution was properly denied.

 

1285 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


McCormick v. Lawrence


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


54 A.D.2d 123; 387 N.Y.S.2d 919; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13734; 6 ELR 20795



October 28, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners builders sought review of the decision of the Supreme Court at Special Term in Essex County (New York), which granted respondent Adirondack Park Agency (agency)'s motion to dismiss and confirmed a determination by the agency prohibiting the constriction by the builders of any boathouse on the shore of the lake within the boundaries of Adirondack Park.


OVERVIEW: The builders petitioned the agency for the construction of part of the parkland. The agency granted the builder a permit on the condition that the builders were not to build boathouses on agency property. The builders filed suit and the trial court granted the agency's motion to dismiss. The builders appealed and on appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court found that both parties presented no actual triable issue of fact. The court also concluded that the agency had authority to ban boathouses on agency administered private property because before the agency approved a project or granted a permit therefor, it was required to find that the project would not have had an adverse impact upon the natural, scenic or aesthetic resources of the park pursuant to N.Y. Exec. Law §809(10)(e). The court concluded that the agency possessed the proper constitutional delegation of power and that their decision was not arbitrary or capricious. The area surrounding the builder's property was in a relatively pristine state and the agency could have reasonably found that the addition of several boathouses would have adversely affected the aesthetic quality of the area.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court and found that no triable issue of fact necessitated a trial was presented, the agency had the authority to ban boathouses on agency administered private property, and the agency's determination was not arbitrary nor capricious when they conditioned the builders project on that no boathouses were to have been built.


HEADNOTES

Environmental conservation -- Adirondack Park Agency -- construction of boathouses.

1. Respondents have authority to ban the construction of boathouses by petitioners on Adirondack Park Agency administered private property. The delegation of power to the agency to impose such conditions in granting a permit as are allowable within the proper exercise of the police power ( Executive Law, § 809, subd 13), which power includes preserving the appearance of an area, is not unconstitutional, the Legislature having provided sufficient standards to guide the agency in the review of projects.

2. The restriction forbidding boathouses was rational since [***2] the area surrounding petitioners' property is in a pristine state and since the subject property fronts on a much traveled pleasure boat route. Accordingly, the determination was not arbitrary, capricious or an abuse of discretion.

3. Special Term was correct in deciding the merits of the petition without a trial. The exhibits, including photographs submitted by both parties, sufficiently demonstrate the general lack of development and the pristine nature of the area, and, therefore, no factual issue was presented.

 

1286 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Pausley v. Chaloner


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


54 A.D.2d 131; 388 N.Y.S.2d 35; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13736



October 28, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, mother and child, filed an action against defendant hospital. Plaintiffs alleged that the hospital negligently treated the child. The Supreme Court, Greene County (New York) dismissed the complaint on the ground that plaintiffs failed to comply with the time requirements of N.Y. County Law § 52 and N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 50-i.


OVERVIEW: The hospital was a municipality within the meaning of N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law §§ 50-e, 50-i. N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 50-e required that notice of a tort claim be served upon a municipality within 90 days after the claim arose. The statute extended the time to a maximum of one year in certain cases. Plaintiffs failed to serve notice within the extended period. However, plaintiffs served their complaint within the three-year statute of limitations. The court held that the notice of claim prerequisite did not deny plaintiffs equal protection or due process. Because the hospital operation was considered a governmental function, plaintiffs were dependent upon legislative grace for their cause of action. Thus, there was no equal protection violation even though the hospital had a shorter time limitation then private hospitals. Additionally, the shortness of the 90-day limitation was not so unreasonable that it violated due process. The mother was presumably aware the child had suffered some injury before 90 days had elapsed because the complaint alleged that the hospital's negligence caused quadriplegia.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of plaintiffs' complaint was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- notice of claim.

1. Plaintiffs brought a medical malpractice action against a hospital operated by Greene County, a municipality within the meaning of sections 50-e and 50-i of the General Municipal Law, within the time allowed by the applicable Statute of Limitations but more than one year after the injury. Section 50-e of the General Municipal Law provides that as a prerequisite to any tort action against a municipality a notice of claim must be served within 90 days after the claim arises. Due to the nature of the injuries, presumably the plaintiff mother was aware of the existence of a claim before 90 days elapsed. Since the operation of a hospital is one of the "governmental" functions of government and the right to sue the government in this capacity is granted as a [***2] matter of legislative grace, the Legislature may withold or condition the right to bring suit as it sees fit. Accordingly, section 50-e is not violative of equal protection, even though there may be no differences between public and private hospitals justifying the requirement.

2. Assuming, arguendo, that once the State waives immunity it must act reasonably in allowing the adjudication of claims, the shortness of the notice period does not violate due process.

 

1287 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Harris


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


54 A.D.2d 739; 387 N.Y.S.2d 661; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14368



October 18, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court of Richmond County (New York), which, upon a jury verdict, convicted him of bail jumping in the first and second degrees when he failed to personally appear, as required, in a criminal court in connection with certain pending felony and misdemeanor charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of bail jumping in the first and second degrees, contending that his right to due process was violated because he was affirmatively required to prove that his nonappearance was not voluntary or willful. On appeal, the court affirmed his conviction, holding that he was not required to carry the burden of proof on an element of bail jumping because failure to appear in court was a crime whether or not he had intended to appear, and it required no culpable mental state. The court concluded that his affirmative defense, alleging that the absence was unavoidable, was solely concerned with why defendant was absent from court and was unconcerned with his state of mind or intent, so the defense was in the nature of a confession and avoidance, with no burden on defendant to establish or negate an essential element of the crime. The court also held that bail jumping in the second degree was not a lesser included crime of bail jumping in the first degree in defendant's case because one was tied exclusively to the existence of a pending misdemeanor charge and the other was tied to a pending felony charge, so the counts were concurrent but noninclusory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of bail jumping in the first and second degrees.

 

1288 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cwikla


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


54 A.D.2d 80; 387 N.Y.S.2d 573; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13616



October 14, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Judgment, Supreme Court, Bronx County, rendered on June 27, 1973, unanimously modified, on the law, to the extent of reversing the conviction on the grand larceny, second degree count, vacating the sentence imposed thereon and dismissing that count of the indictment and, as so modified, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court, Bronx County (New York), upon a verdict convicting defendant of robbery in the first degree and grand larceny in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: The district attorney conceded that under the circumstances, the count of grand larceny in the second degree was a lesser included concurrent count to robbery in the first degree. Defendant's contention that N.Y. Penal Law § 160.15(4) violated due process in that it placed upon him the burden (affirmative defense) of proving that the weapon used in the robbery was not loaded or was inoperable to reduce the charge from robbery in the first degree to the second degree, N.Y. Penal Law § 160.10, was without merit. N.Y. Penal Law § 160.15(4) was not unconstitutional. Placing the burden of proof on defendant as to a fact peculiarly within his knowledge did not deny him the benefit of the presumption of innocence. With respect to the refusal to direct separate trials of defendant on each of the two robberies charged, N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 200.20(2)(c) permitted joinder of similar crimes. On the record no prejudice accrued to defendant from such joinder so as to deprive him of a fair trial. The remaining contentions advanced by defendant were found to be without merit.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment to the extent of reversing the conviction on the grand larceny, second degree count, vacating the sentence imposed thereon and dismissing that count of the indictment and, affirmed the judgment, as modified.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- robbery -- affirmative defense -- subdivision 4 of section 160.15 of Penal Law is constitutional.

1. Subdivision 4 of section 160.15 of the Penal Law which provides that, in a prosecution for robbery in the first degree, it is an affirmative defense that the firearm used was not loaded or was inoperable, is constitutional. (See People v Felder, 39 AD2d 373, 375-379, affd 32 NY2d 747, appeal dismissed sub nom Felder v New York, 414 U.S. 948.)

2. The decision of Mullaney v Wilbur (421 U.S. 684), in which the United States Supreme Court struck down a Maine statute providing that in the case of unlawful homicide, malice was to be implied [***2] unless defendant proved by a fair preponderance of the evidence that he acted in the heat of passion or sudden provocation, does not impel a conclusion that subdivision 4 of section 160.15 is unconstitutional. (See People v Patterson, 39 NY2d 288.)

3. Separate trials of defendant on each of two robberies charged were properly refused. Defendant was not prejudiced from the joinder so as to deprive him of a fair trial.

1290 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Rosenstock v. Scaringe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


54 A.D.2d 779; 387 N.Y.S.2d 716; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14461



October 8, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant candidate sought review of a judgment entered by the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which sustained respondent voter's challenge to her candidacy for a seat on a board of education on the ground that the candidate was ineligible under N.Y. Educ. Law § 2103(3) because her husband was already a member of that board.


OVERVIEW: The candidate was nominated, by petition, as a candidate for a seat on a board of education. The voter commenced an action challenging her candidacy on the ground that she was ineligible under § 2103(3) because her husband was already a member of that board. The trial court sustained the voter's challenge. The candidate appealed from that decision, which was affirmed. Section 2103(3) stated that no more than one member of a family could be a member of the same board of education in any school district. The court found that § 2103(3) did not directly infringe upon the right to vote. Rather, § 2103(3) only indirectly infringed upon that right by making a certain class of citizens ineligible for a public office. Therefore, the scope of review was limited to a determination of whether § 2103(3) was rationally related to the promotion of a legitimate state interest. The court found that § 2103(3) ensured that a board of education would be comprised of a wide cross-section of the community and that issues would be debated free from the inhibition that might exist because of an intimate relationship. Therefore, the court concluded that § 2103(3) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which had granted the voter's petition challenging the candidate's eligibility. No costs were awarded on appeal.

 

1291 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Butler


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


54 A.D.2d 56; 387 N.Y.S.2d 180; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13607



September 24, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Judgments insofar as they impose sentences unanimously reversed on the law and matter remitted to Erie County Court for resentence in accordance with opinion by Goldman, J., and otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgments of the Erie County Court (New York) convicting him of two counts of driving while intoxicated (DWI) and sentencing him to concurrent indeterminate terms with a maximum of three years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with five felony counts of DWI. He pleaded guilty to two counts. Prior to sentencing, the trial court denied defense counsel's request to examine the presentence report based on the fact that it had declared N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 390.50(2) unconstitutional in a case earlier that morning. In imposing defendant's sentence, the trial court read from the presentence report. On appeal, the court reversed defendant's sentence. The state did not press the argument that § 390.50(2) was unconstitutional. The court held that the disclosure provision of § 390.50(2) was mandatory, subject to certain discretionary exceptions. If the report was not disclosed, a statement on the record of the reasons for the nondisclosure was required and appellate review was available. The trial court abused its discretion by making a uniform policy of nondisclosure and refusing absolutely to abide by § 390.50(2).


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's sentence and remitted the matter for resentencing. The court ordered that the presentence report was to be made available to defendant and the trial court was to state for the record any parts of the report withheld and the reasons for its action.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- disclosure -- presentence report.

 CPL 390.50 (subd 2) mandates a sentencing court either to make a presentence report available to a defendant or his counsel, subject to certain discretionary exceptions, or to set forth substantial reasons for nondisclosure. Accordingly, a sentencing court abused its discretion when, taking the position that the statute was unconstitutional, it denied a defense request for disclosure of a presentence report without setting forth any reasons, having specific reference to the particular case, for its refusal to disclose. The sentence imposed by it is vacated and the matter is remitted to it for resentencing, prior to which it should make all or parts of the presentence report available to defendant excepting such [***2] parts as it deems it may properly refuse under the statute, and, if any parts are excepted, it shall state for the record that a part or parts have been excepted and the reasons for its action.

 

1292 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Toia v. Regan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


54 A.D.2d 46; 387 N.Y.S.2d 309; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13606



September 10, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Appeal No. 1 -- Judgment unanimously affirmed without costs and the county officials directed to reimburse the State for funds advanced pursuant to any prior court orders. Leave to appeal to the Court of Appeals granted.

Appeal No. 2 -- Order unanimously dismissed as moot.

 [***2] Appeal No. 3 -- Order unanimously dismissed as moot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent commissioner of the State Department of Social Services (commissioner) sought to compel appellant county officials to appropriate adequate funds for the administration of the home relief, aid to dependent children, medical assistance for needy persons and day care programs in the county under the Social Services Law. The Supreme Court (New York) granted the relief sought. The county officials appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county officials alleged that the 50 percent contribution ratio of the cost to provide aid, care, and support for the needy resulted in the imposition of local taxes in excess of the constitutional limit, violated the right of the county residents to effective self government and home rule, and resulted in a denial of equal protection and due process rights under the federal and state constitutions. The court held that the county officials did not assert or prove that they were taxing real property at the maximum allowable rate. The court held that although the law indirectly touched upon the concerns of individual localities and affected their resolution, the rights of individual counties to govern their local affairs must yield to the state's legislative authority. The court found that the concentration of one half of the non-federal cost at the local level rationally furthers the state's interest in providing the individual counties with a compelling incentive to administer the programs efficiently and to prevent abuses. Therefore, the challenged provisions were rationally related to effectuate the general policy concerning aid, care, and support of the needy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision in favor of the commissioner.


HEADNOTES

Social services -- funding of public assistance programs -- imposition of 50% of non-Federal costs upon county.

A judgment granting a petition by the Commissioner of the New York State Department of Social Services to compel officials of Erie County to appropriate funds for the administration of home relief, aid to dependent children, medical assistance and day care programs in that county, as required by provisions of the Social Services Law, which obligate the county to provide 50% of the non-Federally reimbursed costs of those programs, is affirmed. Absent evidence that the county is currently taxing real property at the maximum allowable rate, it cannot claim that the continued imposition of the 50% contribution rate upon it will force it to impose taxes in excess of the limit set by the New York State Constitution. As to a claim by it that the continued imposition of that contribution rate interferes with its right to self government and home rule, the State Legislature may constitutionally abridge the right of local governments to home rule upon enactment of a valid general law, and the challenged statute, which [***3] applies with equal force to every local government within the State and attempts to regulate the nature and extent of State contribution to local welfare commitments, legitimately a matter of State-wide public concern, is such a general law. Nor does the continued imposition of the 50% contribution rate result in a denial of equal protection or of due process, since the 50% contribution system rationally furthers a legitimate, articulated State purpose and is rationally related to the effectuation of the general policy concerning the aid, care and support of the needy as contained in the New York State Constitution.

 

1293 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Musolino


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


54 A.D.2d 22; 386 N.Y.S.2d 710; 1976 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13086



August 5, 1976 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Sullivan County Court (New York), entered upon a jury verdict, convicting him of murder and attempted murder, N.Y. Penal Law §§ 125.25(1) and 110.00.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder and attempted murder, in violation of N.Y. Penal Law §§ 125.25(1) and 110.00. When he testified at his trial, the prosecutor questioned him about his remaining silent when he was arrested. Defendant's attorney initially objected, but the objection was withdrawn. The prosecutor also impeached his credibility by asking defendant questions suggesting that his attorney had coached him and helped him fabricate an exculpatory story. Defendant was convicted and he appealed, assigning error to the cross-examination and claiming that the prosecutor had also made inflammatory statements during closing arguments. In affirming, the court noted that defendant had failed to make a contemporaneous objection to any of the assigned errors and ruled that the alleged errors did not irreparably taint the trial and were not so pervasive or prejudicial for the court to consider those points as a matter of discretion in the interests of justice. While commenting on any defendant's post-arrest silence was improper, that and the other errors were harmless. The proof of defendant's guilt was strong and his testimony lacked credibility.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed because defendant failed to preserve for appeal the issues of the prosecutor's improper questioning of him on cross-examination about his post-arrest silence and alleged inflammatory comments made during summation. The unobjected-to errors did not irreparably taint the trial such that they should nevertheless be reviewed in the interests of justice.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- right to remain silent -- on cross-examination of defendant, where defense counsel failed to preserve for review question whether it was proper to use defendant's post-arrest silence to impeach his testimony, error did not so vary from lawful procedure that entire trial was irreparably tainted, thereby mandating reversal -- defendant's conviction may not be reversed on such error as matter of discretion in interest of justice since proof of guilt was strong, error only served to impeach incredible story, and impeachment impact of post-arrest silence was mild -- efforts to impeach defendant on cross-examination by asking how long defendant conferred with his attorney in preparing to testify did not violate his right to counsel -- defendant's conviction of murder and attempted murder is, accordingly, affirmed.

1. On cross-examination of defendant in a prosecution for murder and attempted murder, where defense counsel failed to preserve for review the question of whether [***2] it was proper to use defendant's post-arrest silence to impeach his testimony, the error did not so vary from lawful procedure that the entire trial was irreparably tainted, thereby mandating reversal. The erroneous cross-examination placed improper evidence before the jury, but it did not warp the rules of procedure by which the other evidence was to be evaluated.

2. The conviction of defendant may not be reversed on such error as a matter of discretion in the interest of justice. The proof of guilt was strong, the error only served to impeach what was very nearly an incredible story by defendant ab initio, and the impeachment impact of defendant's post-arrest silence was mild.

3. The prosecutor's efforts to impeach defendant on cross-examinaion by asking how long he had conferred with his attorney in preparing to testify did not violate his Sixth Amendment right to counsel. Comment on consultation with his attorney is permissible when it induces defendant to admit he was coached. However, even if it was improper for the prosecutor in summation to question defendant's credibility by pointing to a 4 1/2 hour session, such comment was harmless as it only tended to discredit [***3] a story which could hardly be believed.

4. No objection was made to two other portions of the prosecutor's closing argument and they do not require reversal in the interest of justice.

5. Accordingly, the judgment convicting defendant of murder and attempted murder should be affirmed.
